Chapter Three: Discrepancy in Chain and Text. Al-Nasa'i also narrated it via al-Walid ibn Muslim and Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, both from Ibn Jurayj, from Abdullah ibn Musafi', from Utbah ibn Muhammad, from Abdullah ibn Ja'far, with the wording: 'after he salams', and in some versions: 'after the salam'. And Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Mizzi narrated it via Hajjaj, and Ahmad narrated it via Rawh. Both from Ibn Jurayj from Abdullah ibn Musafi', from Mus'ab ibn Shaybah, from Utbah ibn Muhammad, from Abdullah ibn Ja'far, with the wording: 'after he salams', and in some versions: 'after he makes salam'. So this hadith is ambiguous in its wording: 'while he is sitting'. It is understood from it that it is before the salam, and the other narration: 'after he salams'. The effect of this hadith on the disagreement of jurists: Ruling on doubt in the number of Rak'ahs in prayer. If someone doubts in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed two or three, or three or four, or one or two, what should he do? There is disagreement among scholars on opinions: The first opinion: A group of jurists holds that whoever doubts in his prayer, increase or decrease in the number of rak'ahs, should build on his predominant suspicion. This is narrated from Anas ibn Malik, Abu Zayd al-Ansari, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Hasan al-Basri, and 'Ata'. And it is the madhhab of the Zahiriyyah. Their proof: the previous hadith, and the hadith of Abu Hurayrah marfu': 'If one of you does not know whether he prayed three or four, let him prostrate two prostrations while he is sitting', and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud marfu': 'I am only a human, so if I forget, remind me. If one of you is uncertain in his prayer, let him try to determine what is closest to correctness, then complete it, then prostrate two prostrations.' The second opinion: It is the saying of Imam Ahmad - a distinction between the imam and the ma'mum, and in both cases there are two narrations. Al-Athram narrated from him that the imam builds on predominant suspicion, and there is another narration of building on certainty, which Abu al-Khattab corrected. As for the individual or the ma'mum, they build on...
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis showing how a minor wording variation in a hadith leads to different fiqh rulings. The hadith in question concerns doubt in the number of prayer rak'ahs. One narration says 'while he is sitting' (وهو جالس), implying the prostrations are done before the taslim, while another says 'after he salams' (بعدما يسلم), implying after. This ambiguity affects the ruling: the first opinion (Zahiriyyah and others) builds on predominant suspicion, using the hadith as proof that one should act on the most likely number. The second opinion (Imam Ahmad) distinguishes between imam and ma'mum, with both opinions having variant transmissions. The Hanafi position (not detailed here) is to build on certainty (the lesser number). The passage highlights how textual differences in the same hadith directly impact legal differences.

Key Terms
غالب الظن (ghalib al-dhann): Predominant suspicion: the stronger belief based on evidence, not certainty.
البناء على اليقين (al-bina' 'ala al-yaqeen): Building on certainty: relying on what is certain (the lesser number) and treating doubt as non-existent.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt: equal possibility between two alternatives, without preponderance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the wording difference in the hadith about doubt in prayer (e.g., 'while sitting' vs. 'after he salams') affect the fiqh ruling?
A) It does not affect the ruling; both wordings support the same opinion.
B) It leads to a difference: the first opinion (Zahiriyyah) uses 'while sitting' to support acting on predominant suspicion, while the wording 'after he salams' is used by others to support building on certainty.
C) It only affects the position of the imam vs. ma'mum, not the general ruling.
D) It changes the number of prostrations required.

Key Takeaway
The wording of a hadith directly impacts the legal ruling, as seen in the dispute over doubt in prayer: 'while sitting' supports predominant suspicion, 'after salams' supports certainty.

The Definition of Ziyadat al-Thiqa and Its Criteria
Introduces the topic and defines ziyadat al-thiqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ziyadat al-thiqa and apply the criterion that a single addition by a trustworthy narrator does not impugn his credibility, while frequent additions raise concern.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's unique addition is not automatically rejected, but frequent additions undermine precision.

In hadith criticism, additions to chains or texts are common and often reveal the skills of scholars. The key is to evaluate who makes the addition and how often. This lesson defines 'ziyadat al-thiqa' and explains the rule: a single addition by a reliable narrator does not impugn his truthfulness, but frequent contradictions do. Understanding this principle is essential for distinguishing acceptable from problematic narrations.

Guided Path
1
Define ziyadat al-thiqa
Identify the definition from the passage: what the reliable narrator uniquely reports, a word or phrase, in sanad or matn.
The definition specifies that the addition must be unique to that narrator.
2
Understand the condition of uniqueness
The addition must be exclusive to that narrator; if others also report it, it is not a ziyada.
Uniqueness is a necessary condition for calling it an addition.
3
Apply the rule about single vs frequent additions
A single addition does not damage credibility, but frequent additions indicate lack of precision (dabt).
The passage cites Ibn Hajar: if a thiqa reports something from a gathering that others could not have missed, his solitary report is not a mark against him.
4
Evaluate the example of Hajjaj ibn Artah
Ahmad ibn Hanbal praised his memory but criticized his frequent additions, illustrating that frequency undermines reliability.
This example shows the practical application of the criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن والثَّوْرِيّ ، وإليه ذهب المالكية، والشافعية.
والحجة لأصحاب هَذَا القَوْل مَا صَحَّ عن أبي سعيد الخُدْرِيّ؛ أَن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فَلَمْ يدركم صلى فليبنِ عَلَى اليَقِيْنِ، حَتَّى إذا استيقن أن قَدْ أتم فليسجد سجدتين).
تمهید
المبحث الثاني: الاختلاف في الزيادات
الزيادات الواقعة في المتون أو الأسانيد لَها أهمية بالغة عِنْدَ عُلَمَاء الحَدِيث؛ إذ أن لَهَا عندهم مجال نظر وبحث واسع. وَلَمْ يَكُنْ أمرها عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ اعتباطياً، ثُمَّ إِن الزيادات الواردة في المتون أو الأسانيد قد كشفت عن قدرات المتكلمين فيها، وأبانت عن قدرات محدّثي الأمة وصيارفة الحَدِيث في النقد والتعليل والكشف والتصحيح
والتضعيف.
والزيادات الواردة في بغض الأماكن دُونَ بَعْض نَوْع من أنواع الاختلاف سَوَاء كَانَ في المَتْن أم في السَّنَد. ومَعْرِفَة الزيادات هي إحدى قضايا علل الحَدِيث الَّتِي مرجعها إلى الاختلاف بالروايات واختلاف الرواة في بعض الأحايين سنداً أو متناً أمرٌ طبيعي ولا غرابة فيهِ إذ إن الرواة يبعد أن يكونوا جميعاً في مستوى واحد من التيقظ والضَّبْط والحفظ، وليسوا في مستوى واحد من الاهتمام والتثبت والدقة. واختلاف المقدار قَدْ يَكُون مداه طويلاً من حين تلقي الأحاديث من أصحابها إلى حِيْنَ أدائها، إذ إن شرط الضَّبْط أن يَكُون من حِيْن التحمل إلى حين الأداء)، وما دامت المواهب متفاوتة حفظاً وضبطاً فإن الاختلاف في الزيادات وارد لا محالة. فالرواة مِنْهُمْ من بَلَغَ أعلى مراتب الحفظ والإتقان، ومنهم دُونَ ذَلِكَ ومنهم أدنى بكثير. ثُمَّ إن الرواة كثيراً ما يشتركون في سَمَاع الحَدِيث الواحد من شيخ واحد، فحين يحدّثون بهذا الحَدِيث بَعْدَ فترة من الزمن يَكُون الاختلاف بينهم بحسب مقدار حفظهم وتيقظهم وتثبتهم.
عَلَى أن أحد الرواة الثّقات لَوْ زاد زيادة لم تكن عِنْدَ البقية فإن ذَلِكَ لا يَقْدَح بصدقه وعدالته وضبطه، قال الحافظ ابن حجر: إن الواحد الثّقة إذا كَانَ في مجلس جَمَاعَة، ثُمَّ ذكر عن ذَلِكَ المجلس شيئاً لا يمكن غفلتهم عَنْهُ، وَلَمْ يذكره غيره، إِن ذَلِكَ لا يَقْدَح في صدقه. إلا إذا كثر ذَلِكَ مِنْهُ فإنه مجال بحث ونظر عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ، فمن أكثر من ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مكثر من المخالفة، وكثرة المخالفة منافية للضبط ، إذ إن الضبط يعرف بموافقة الرَّاوِي للثقات الضابطين (). ومن ذَلِكَ مَا نقل عن الإمام أحمد بن حَنْبَل في ترجمة حجاج بن أرطاة، فَقَدْ قَالَ أبو طالب عن أحمد بن حَنْبَل كَانَ من الحفاظ. قِيلَ: فَلِمَ لَيْسَ هُوَ عِنْدَ الناس بذاك؟ قَالَ: لأن في حديثه زيادة عَلَى حَدِيث الناسِ، لَيْسَ يكاد لَهُ حديث إلا فيه زيادة.
ثُمَّ إن مَعْرِفَة الزيادات تكون بجمع الطرق والأبواب والزيادات الَّتِي هِي مجال نظر وبحث إنما هِيَ الَّتِي تَكُون من بَعْدِ الصَّحَابَة، أما من الصَّحَابَة فهي مقبولة اتفاقاً. والزيادات في الأحاديث تكون من الثّقات ومن الضعفاء، والزيادة من الضَّعِيف غير مقبولة؛ لأن حديثه مردود أصلاً سَوَاء زاد أم لَمْ يزد. أما الزيادة من الثّقة فهي مجال بحثنا هنا.
وَقَدْ قسمت الْحَدِيث عَنْهَا في مطالب.
المطلب الأول: تعريفها
وزيادة الثقة: هِيَ مَا يتفرد بِهِ النّقَة في رِوَايَة الحَدِيث من لفظة أو جملة في السَّنَد
أو المثن.
Chapter Three / Disagreement in Sanad and Matn and al-Thawri, and to this the Malikis and Shafi'is went. The proof for the proponents of this statement is what is authentically reported from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'If any of you doubts his prayer and does not know how many he has prayed, let him build on certainty, until he is certain that he has completed, then let him prostrate two prostrations.' Introduction: The Second Section: Disagreement in Additions. Additions occurring in texts or chains have great importance with hadith scholars, as they have a wide field of consideration and research. Their matter was not arbitrary with the muhaddithin. Then, additions reported in texts or chains have revealed the abilities of those who speak about them, and have shown the abilities of the hadith scholars of the ummah and the expert critics of hadith in criticism, defect identification, discovery, authentication, and weakening. The additions reported in some places but not others are a type of disagreement, whether in the text or the chain. Knowledge of additions is one of the issues of hadith defects, the reference of which is to disagreement in narrations. Disagreement among narrators in some cases, in chain or text, is natural and not strange, since it is unlikely that all narrators are at the same level of vigilance, precision, and memory, and they are not at the same level of attention, verification, and accuracy. The extent of difference may be long from the time of receiving hadith from their sources to the time of performance, since the condition of precision is that it be from the time of reception to the time of performance. As long as talents differ in memory and precision, disagreement in additions is inevitable. So among the narrators are those who reached the highest levels of memory and mastery, and others below that, and others much lower. Then, narrators often share in hearing one hadith from one shaykh, so when they transmit this hadith after a period of time, there is disagreement among them according to the extent of their memory, vigilance, and verification. Moreover, if one trustworthy narrator adds an addition that others did not have, that does not impugn his truthfulness, integrity, and precision. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'If a trustworthy individual is in a gathering of a group, then he mentions something about that gathering that they could not have been heedless of, and no one else mentioned it, that does not impugn his truthfulness.' Unless that becomes frequent from him, then it is a field of discussion and consideration with the muhaddithin. Whoever does that frequently is one who frequently contradicts, and frequent contradiction is contrary to precision, since precision is known by the narrator's agreement with trustworthy precise narrators. An example of that is what is transmitted from Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal in the biography of Hajjaj ibn Artah. Abu Talib reported from Ahmad ibn Hanbal: 'He was among the preservers of hadith.' It was said: 'Then why is he not considered such by people?' He said: 'Because in his hadith there is addition over people's hadith; there is hardly a hadith of his except that it has an addition.' Then, knowledge of additions is by collecting the chains and chapters. The additions that are a field of consideration and research are only those that occur after the Companions. As for those from the Companions, they are acceptable by agreement. Additions in hadith come from trustworthy and weak narrators. The addition from a weak narrator is not acceptable because his hadith is rejected fundamentally, whether he adds or not. As for the addition from a trustworthy narrator, it is the subject of our discussion here. And I have divided the discussion about it into sections. The First Section: Its Definition. Addition of the trustworthy (ziyadat al-thiqa): it is what the reliable narrator uniquely reports in the narration of a hadith, of a word or a sentence, in the chain or the text.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a methodological introduction to the topic of ziyadat (additions) in hadith, specifically those made by trustworthy narrators (thiqat). The author first mentions a fiqh ruling supported by a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri—that one who doubts in prayer should build on certainty and then prostrate for forgetfulness—and notes that it is held by Hanafis, Malikis, and Shafi'is. This hadith is provided as evidence, but the main focus shifts to the second section on disagreement in ziyadat. The author emphasizes that additions in matn or sanad are a significant area of hadith criticism, revealing the skills of scholars in evaluating and authenticating reports. He asserts that variation in narrations is natural due to differences in narrators' memory, precision, and vigilance. Importantly, he states that a single addition by a trustworthy narrator that others did not report does not necessarily impugn his truthfulness or precision, citing Ibn Hajar's principle: if a thiqa reports something from a gathering that others could not have missed, his solitary report is not a mark against him. However, frequent additions raise concern, as they indicate a habit of contradicting other reliable narrators, which undermines precision (dabt). The author illustrates this with the example of Hajjaj ibn Artah, praised by Ahmad ibn Hanbal for his memory but criticized for having additions in nearly every hadith. Finally, the author clarifies that additions from Companions are universally accepted, while additions from weak narrators are rejected because their hadith is already invalid. The focus here is on additions from trustworthy narrators, which he defines as: a word or phrase that a reliable narrator uniquely reports in the chain or text of a hadith. This definition sets the stage for further discussion in subsequent sections.

Key Terms
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): What the reliable narrator uniquely reports in the narration of a hadith, of a word or a sentence, in the chain or the text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements is true about a trustworthy narrator who frequently adds unique content to hadiths?
A) His additions are accepted because he is trustworthy.
B) His additions are rejected due to frequent contradiction undermining his precision.
C) His additions are considered on a case-by-case basis without any pattern.
D) His additions are accepted only if he is a Companion.

Key Takeaway
A single addition by a trustworthy narrator is not a sign of unreliability, but frequent additions weaken his credibility and require rejection.

Ziyadat al-Thiqa: Definition, Divisions, and Ruling
Defines and classifies ziyadat al-thiqa with usul rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ziyadat al-thiqa, distinguish its two divisions, and evaluate the Hanafi usul ruling on its acceptance based on the session (majlis) condition.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's unique addition is accepted in principle, but its acceptance depends on the session of hearing and frequency of contradictions.

In this lesson, we delve into ziyadat al-thiqa, a key concept in hadith criticism that affects how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from narrations. You will learn the definition, divisions, and the scholarly disagreement on acceptance, especially when the session of hearing is unknown. This understanding is crucial for evaluating conflicting hadith and applying proper istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Define ziyadat al-thiqa
Identify the key components: a unique addition (word or phrase) by a trustworthy narrator in either the sanad or matn, not narrated by others.
Note the condition that the narrator must be thiqah; additions from weak narrators are rejected outright.
2
Distinguish the two divisions
Separate additions in the sanad (e.g., connecting a mursal hadith) from additions in the matn (extra wording). Recall that additions from the Companions are accepted by consensus.
Frequent additions (mukhalafah) indicate weak dabt and may lead to rejection.
3
Analyze the ruling based on the session (majlis)
Consider the three scenarios: (A) session differs – accepted due to possibility of separate hearing; (B) session unknown – scholars differ (al-Abyari: accepted; al-Hindi: should be accepted; al-Amidi: accepted with preference; Abu al-Husayn: hesitation/tarjih); (C) session same – not explicitly discussed but implies need for careful scrutiny.
Al-Zarkashi refutes the claim of consensus on scenario A.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
Recognize that the Hanafi approach favors acceptance when the session differs, and leans toward acceptance when unknown, relying on the principle that the trustworthy narrator is presumed correct unless counterevidence exists.
This aligns with the usul principle that certainty (yaqin) is not overridden by doubt (shakk).

يحدّثون بهذا الحَدِيث بَعْدَ فترة من الزمن يَكُون الاختلاف بينهم بحسب مقدار حفظهم وتيقظهم وتثبتهم.
عَلَى أن أحد الرواة الثّقات لَوْ زاد زيادة لم تكن عِنْدَ البقية فإن ذَلِكَ لا يَقْدَح بصدقه وعدالته وضبطه، قال الحافظ ابن حجر: إن الواحد الثّقة إذا كَانَ في مجلس جَمَاعَة، ثُمَّ ذكر عن ذَلِكَ المجلس شيئاً لا يمكن غفلتهم عَنْهُ، وَلَمْ يذكره غيره، إِن ذَلِكَ لا يَقْدَح في صدقه (۱). إلا إذا كثر ذَلِكَ مِنْهُ فإنه مجال بحث ونظر عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ، فمن أكثر من ذَلِكَ فَهُوَ مكثر من المخالفة، وكثرة المخالفة منافية للضبط، إذ إن الضبط يعرف بموافقة الرَّاوِي للثقات الضابطين (). ومن ذَلِكَ مَا نقل عن الإمام أحمد بن حَنْبَل في ترجمة حجاج بن أرطاة، فَقَدْ قَالَ أبو طالب عن أحمد بن حَنْبَل كَانَ من الحفاظ. قِيلَ: فَلِمَ لَيْسَ هُوَ عِنْدَ الناس بذاك؟ قَالَ: لأن في حديثه زيادة عَلَى حَدِيث الناسِ، لَيْسَ يكاد لَهُ حديث إلا فيه زيادة (۳).

المطلب الثالث: حكم زيادة الثقة
إن الزيادة في المثن إذا جاءت من الثَّقَة فَلا تخرج الرّوَايَة عن ثلاثة أمور: أ. أن يختلف المجلس، أي مجلس السَّماع فتقبل الرّوَايَة الزائدة إذا اختلف المجلس لاحتمال سَمَاع الرَّاوِي لهذه الزيادة في مجلس لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ أَحَدٌ مِمَّنْ سَمِعَ الحَدِيث في المجلس الأول، وَقَالَ الزَّرْكَشِيّ: «زعم الأبياري وابن الحاجب والهندي وغيرهم أَنَّهُ لا خِلاف في هَذَا القِسْم، وَلَيْسَ كَذلِكَ».
ب. أن لا يعلم الحال هَلْ تعدد المجلس أم اتحد، فألحقها الأبياري بالتي قبلها أي تقبل بلا خلاف، وَقَالَ الهندي: ينبغي أن يَكُون فِيْهَا خِلاف يترتب على الخلاف في الاتحاد وأولى بالقبول؛ لأن المقتضي لتصديقه حاصل والمعارض لَهُ غَيْـر محقق، وَقَالَ الآمدي : حكمه حكم المتحد وأولى بالقبول؛ نظراً إلى احتمال التعدد، وأشار أبو الْحُسَيْن في " المعتمد () إلى التوقف والرجوع إلى الترجيح ثُمَّ قَالَ: والصَّحِيح أن يقال: يَجِبُ حمل الخبرين عَلَى أنهما جريا في مجلسين. وَقَالَ
(۱) وقد سبق الكلام أن مِثْل هَذَا الاختلاف لا يَقْدَح في الرواة إلا إذا كثر، قال الخطيب في الكفاية ٤١١: «لأن إرسال الراويللحديث لَيْسَ بجرح لِمَنْ وصله ولا تكذيب له، ولعله أيضاً مسند عِنْدَ الذين رووه مرسلاً أو عند بعضهم، إلا أنهم أرسلوه لغرض أو نسيان، والناسي لا يقضي لَهُ عَلَى الذاكر، وَكَذَلِكَ حال راوي الخبر إذا أرسله مرة ووصله أخرى لا يضعف ذَلِكَ أيضاً لَهُ؛ لأنه قد ينسى فيرسله، ثُمَّ يذكر بعده فيسنده أو يفعل الأمرين معاً عن قصد مِنْهُ لغرض لَهُ فِيهِ. (۲) انظر : شرح التبصرة (٢١٤/١) ط العلمية (٢٦٥/١) طبعتنا ، وفتح الباقي (٢١٤/١) ط العلمية، (١/

Chapter Three: Disagreement in Sanad and Matn. They relate this hadith after a period of time, and the disagreement among them is according to the extent of their memory, vigilance, and verification. However, if one of the trustworthy narrators adds an addition not found with the rest, then that does not impugn his truthfulness, uprightness, and accuracy. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'If a trustworthy person is in a gathering of a group, then he mentions about that gathering something that they could not have been unaware of, and no one else mentioned it, then that does not impugn his truthfulness' (1). Except if such [additions] are numerous from him, then it is a subject of discussion and consideration among hadith scholars. For whoever does that often is one who frequently contradicts [others], and frequent contradiction is inconsistent with accuracy, because accuracy is known by the narrator's agreement with trustworthy and accurate narrators (2). Among that is what is transmitted from Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal regarding the biography of Hajjaj ibn Artah: Abu Talib said from Ahmad ibn Hanbal: 'He was one of the memorizers.' He was asked: 'Why then is he not considered so among the people?' He said: 'Because in his hadith there is an addition over the hadith of others, and there is hardly any hadith of his except that there is an addition in it' (3). Then, knowledge of additions is achieved by collecting all the chains (turuq) and sections (abwab). The additions that are subject to consideration and discussion are only those that occur after the Companions. As for those from the Companions, they are accepted by consensus (4). Additions in hadith come from trustworthy narrators and from weak narrators. The addition from a weak narrator is not accepted because his hadith is rejected as a whole, whether he added or not (5). As for the addition from a trustworthy narrator, it is the subject of our discussion here. And I have divided the discussion about it into sections. First Section: Its Definition. And ziyadat al-thiqa (addition of a trustworthy narrator) is: what the trustworthy narrator uniquely narrates in a hadith, whether a word or a sentence, in the sanad or the matn. (Footnotes omitted in translation for brevity). 

Chapter Three: Disagreement in Sanad and Matn, Second Section: Divisions of Ziyadat al-Thiqa. According to this definition, it divides into two types: First type: Addition in the sanad, and this often occurs when narrators differ in connecting or disconnecting (irsal) the hadith, similarly in raising (raf') or stopping (waqf) it, or adding a narrator. Second type: It is when one narrator relates an addition of a word or sentence in the text of the hadith that no one else relates (3). Since I have provided illumination about ziyadat al-thiqa, I will now discuss the schools of scholars regarding rejecting or accepting ziyadat al-thiqa. 

Third Section: The Ruling on Ziyadat al-Thiqa. Indeed, the addition in the matn, when it comes from a trustworthy narrator, the narration is limited to three possibilities: A. That the session (majlis) differs, i.e., the session of hearing. Then the addition is accepted if the session differs, because of the possibility that the narrator heard this addition in a session in which none of those who heard the hadith in the first session were present. Al-Zarkashi said: 'Al-Abyari, Ibn al-Hajib, al-Hindi, and others claimed that there is no disagreement in this type, but it is not so.' B. That the situation is unknown whether the session was multiple or single. Al-Abyari included this under the previous [type], i.e., accepted without disagreement. Al-Hindi said: 'It should have disagreement consequential upon the disagreement on unity [of session], and it is more deserving of acceptance because the reason for believing him is present and the counterargument is not confirmed.' Al-Amidi said: 'Its ruling is the same as that of the unified [session] and more deserving of acceptance, considering the possibility of multiplicity.' Abu al-Husayn in al-Mu'tamad (5) indicated hesitation and resort to weighing (tarjih). Then he said: 'The correct view is that it is necessary to assume that the two reports occurred in two sessions.' And he said: (1) The discussion has preceded that such disagreement does not impugn the narrator except when frequent. Al-Khatib said in al-Kifaya: 'Because the narrator's sending (irsal) of a hadith is not a disparagement of the one who connects it nor a falsification of him, and perhaps it is also connected with those who narrated it as mursal or with some of them, except that they sent it for a purpose or out of forgetfulness, and the forgetful person is not judged over the mindful one. Similarly, the case of a narrator who sometimes sends a report and sometimes connects it does not weaken him either, because he may forget and send it, then remember later and connect it, or he may do both intentionally for some purpose he has.' (2) References omitted. (3) See: al-Bahr al-Muhit 4/329, and the matter is as al-Zarkashi said. (4) al-Bahr al-Muhit 4/330 (5) al-Mu'tamad 2/614.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the concept of 'ziyadat al-thiqa' (addition by a trustworthy narrator) within the context of hadith criticism and its impact on fiqh rulings. The author begins by acknowledging that minor additions from trustworthy narrators do not undermine their credibility, citing Ibn Hajar, but warns that frequent additions (mukhalafah) indicate lack of precision (dabt), as seen in Ahmad ibn Hanbal's critique of Hajjaj ibn Artah. The focus then narrows to additions that occur after the Companions' era (since additions from Companions are accepted by consensus), distinguishing between additions from weak narrators (rejected outright) and trustworthy ones (the subject of this chapter). The author defines 'ziyadat al-thiqa' as a unique word or phrase in sanad or matn narrated only by that trustworthy narrator. He then divides it into two categories: additions in the sanad (e.g., connecting a mursal hadith) and additions in the matn (extra wording). Finally, he discusses the ruling on such additions when the session of hearing is different, unknown, or single, citing various usul scholars: al-Zarkashi refutes the claim of consensus on acceptance when sessions differ; al-Abyari, al-Hindi, al-Amidi, and Abu al-Husayn offer nuanced positions. The passage illustrates the careful methodology in evaluating narrations for usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): What a trustworthy narrator uniquely narrates in a hadith, whether a word or sentence, in the sanad or matn.
المخالفة (al-mukhalafah): Contradiction or inconsistency between a narrator’s report and those of other trustworthy narrators.
المجلس (al-majlis): The session of hearing a hadith; whether the addition was heard in the same or different session affects acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is rejected because it differs from others
B) It is accepted because the narrator may have heard it in another session
C) It is suspended until weighing (tarjih)
D) It is accepted only if the narrator is a Companion

Key Takeaway
Ziyadat al-thiqa is a nuanced concept; acceptance depends on the narrator's reliability, frequency of contradictions, and the session of hearing.

The Hanafi Position on Accepting an Addition (Ziyada) to a Hadith
Discusses conditions for accepting or rejecting a ziyada from a trustworthy narrator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ziyada and apply the criteria of majlis and numerical strength to determine acceptance of an addition from a trustworthy narrator.

Core Idea
A ziyada is not automatically accepted; it is rejected unless supported by majority or strong precision.

When a trustworthy narrator adds a word or phrase to a hadith that other reliable narrators omit, should the addition be accepted? This is a foundational dispute in usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi school generally takes a cautious stance, rejecting the ziyada absolutely, while other schools accept it. This lesson unpacks the arguments and introduces the nuanced criteria developed by later scholars to resolve specific cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
Recognize that the core question is whether a ziyada from a thiqah narrator, not reported by others, is accepted. The Hanafi position is absolute rejection; the Shafi'i position accepts it.
The Hanafi view is rooted in the principle that the majority's silence indicates the addition is likely an error.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Proof
Understand the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i analogy with shadhdha qira'a: Quran is tawatur, hadith are ahad. The majority's omission outweighs a single narrator's addition.
This is a key argument distinguishing between tawatur and ahad.
3
Apply the Majlis Criterion
Ibn Daqiq al-'Id and Ibn al-Sabbagh introduce the transmission session (majlis). If narrators heard the hadith together, the majority's version is preferred; if separate sessions, multiple reports.
The majlis helps determine whether the addition is an independent report or a deviation.
4
Use Numerical and Precision Criteria
When numbers are equal, precision (dabt) decides. If both are equally precise, the addition is preferred (Ibn al-Sabbagh). Al-Amidi adds that if the omitting group is too large to have missed it, reject; otherwise accept.
These criteria refine the absolute rejection into a context-sensitive evaluation.

Source Text

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وغيرهم ) وذهبوا إلى أن الرَّاوِي إذا انفرد برواية خبر واحد دُوْنَ الثقات قُبِلَ ذَلِكَ الخبر مِنْه، فكذلك الزيادة؛ لأنه عدل.
٣- وَقِيلَ : لا تقبل الزيادة مطلقاً وهذا ما نقل عن معظم الحنفية، وعزاه السمعاني لبعض أهل الحَدِيث، وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي من تناقض القَوْل الجمع بَيْنَ قبول رِوَايَة القراءة الشاذة في القُرْآن ورد الزيادة الَّتِي ينفرد بِهَا بَعْض الرواة، وحق القُرْآن أن ينقل تواتراً بخلاف الأخبار. وما كَانَ أصله التواتر وقبل فيه زيادة الواحد، فلأن يقبل فيه ما سواه الآحاد أولى وحكاه الْقَاضِي عَبْد الوهاب (۳) عن أبي بَكْر الأبهري وغيره من أصحابهم ) . وَقِيلَ: لا تقبل من الثّقة إذا كَانَتْ من جهته، أي أَنَّهُ رَواهُ ناقصاً ثُمَّ رَواهُ بالزيادة، وتقبل من غيره من الثّقات، وَهُوَ قَوْل جَمَاعَة من الشافعية كما حكاه الخطيب (٤). - ذهب ابن دقيق العيد إلى أَنَّهُ إذا اتحد المجلس فالقول للأكثر ، سَوَاء كانوا رواة الزيادة أو غيرهم، تغليباً لجانب الكثرة فإنها عن الخطأ أبعد، فإن استووا قُدِّمَ الأحفظ والأضبط، فإن استووا قُدِّمَ المثبت عَلَى النافي، وَقِيلَ: النافي؛ لأن الأصل عدمها. والتحقيق أن الزيادة إن نافت المزيد عَلَيْهِ احتج للترجيح لتعذر الجمع... وإن لَمْ تنافه لم يحتج إلى الترجيح، بَلْ يعمل بالزيادة إذا أثبتت كَمَا في المطلق والمقيد (). قال أبو نصر بن الصباغ ): «إذَا رَوَى خبراً واحداً راويان فذكر أحدهما زيادة في خبره لم يروها الآخر، نظرت فإن رويا ذَلِكَ عن مجلسين كانا خبرين وعمل بهما وإن رويا ذَلِكَ عن مجلس واحد فَهُوَ خبر واحد، فإن كَانَ الَّذِي نقل الزيادة واحداً والباقون جَمَاعَة لا يجوز عَلَيْهِمْ الوهم، سقطت الزيادة؛ لأنه لا يجوز أن يَسْمَع جَمَاعَة كلاماً واحداً فيحفظ الواحد ويهم الجماعة، وإن كَانَ الذين نقلوا الزيادة عدداً كبيراً، فالزيادة مقبولة، وإن كَانَ الَّذِي رَوَى الزيادة واحداً والذي سكت عَنْهَا واحداً أيضاً فإن كَانَ الَّذِي رَوَى الزيادة معروفاً بقلة الضَّبْط كَانَ مَا رَواهُ المعروف بالضبط أولى، وإن كَانَا ضابطين ثقتين كَانَ الأخذ بالزيادة)).
وَقَالَ الآمدي (٢): «إن كَانَ من لَمْ يرو الزيادة قد انتهوا إلى عدد لا يتصور في العادة غفلة مثلهم عن سَمَاع تِلْكَ الزيادة وفهمها، فلا يخفى إن تطرق الغلط والسهو إلى واحد فِيْمَا نقله من الزيادة يَكُون أولى من تطرق ذَلِكَ إلى العدد المفروض فيجب ردها، وإن لَمْ ينتهوا إلى هَذَا الحد فَقَدْ اتفق جَمَاعَة الفُقَهَاء والمتكلمين على وجوب قبول الزيادة، خلافاً لجماعة من المُحَدِّثِيْنَ ولأحمد بن حَنْبَل في إحدى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عَنْهُ (۳).
وذهب إلى هَذَا القَوْل ابن الحاجب ) والقرافي وغيرهما)، وَقَالَ أبو الخطاب الكلوذاني: «إن كَانَ ناقل الزيادة جَمَاعَة كثيرة فالزيادة مقبولة والواحد قد وهم، وإن قَدْ كَانَ راوي الزيادة واحداً وراوي النقصان واحداً قدّم أشهرهما بالحفظ والضبط والثّقة، وإِن كَانَا سواءٌ فِي جَمِيْعَ ذَلِكَ فذكر شَيْخُنَا ) عن أحمد رِوَايَتَيْن: أحدهما: أن الأخذ بالزيادة أولى، قَالَهُ في رِوَايَة أحمد بن قاسم قال عامة الفُقَهَاء والمتكلمين والأخرى الزيادة مطروحة. أومأ إليه في رِوَايَة المروذي وأبي طالب، وبه
Chapter Three / Discrepancy in Sanad and Matn. (Others) held that when a narrator uniquely transmits a khabar wahid without the trustworthy narrators, that report is accepted from him, and likewise the addition (ziyada) because he is trustworthy. 3- It is said: The addition is not accepted absolutely, and this is reported from the majority of Hanafis, and al-Sam'ani attributed it to some hadith scholars. Al-Shafi'i said: It is contradictory to combine accepting the narration of the irregular (shadhdha) reading in the Quran and rejecting the addition that some narrators uniquely transmit; but the Quran must be transmitted tawatur unlike reports. And what is originally tawatur, if the addition of one is accepted, then to accept therein what is other than ahad reports is more appropriate. Al-Qadi 'Abd al-Wahhab narrated it from Abu Bakr al-Abhari and others of their companions. And it is said: It is not accepted from the trustworthy if it is from his own side, i.e., he narrated it deficiently then narrated it with the addition, but it is accepted from other trustworthy narrators; and this is the saying of a group of Shafi'is as al-Khatib narrated. Ibn Daqiq al-'Id held that if the session is one, then the majority prevails, whether they are narrators of the addition or others, favoring the side of multiplicity for it is further from error. If they are equal, the most memorizing and precise is given precedence; if equal, the one affirming is given precedence over the one negating, and it is said: the one negating because the original is absence. The investigation: if the addition contradicts the added-to, then resort is made to weighting (tarjih) because combination is impossible... If there is no contradiction, then no need for weighting, rather the addition is acted upon if proven, like in the mutlaq and muqayyad. Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh said: 'When two narrators narrate one report and one of them mentions an addition in his narration that the other did not narrate, then: if they narrated that from two sessions, they are two reports and acted upon accordingly; if from one session, it is one report. If the one who transmitted the addition is single and the rest are a group upon whom error is not conceivable, the addition falls because it is not permissible that a group hears one statement and one preserves it while the group errs. If those who transmitted the addition are a large number, the addition is accepted. If the one who narrated the addition is single and the one silent about it is also single, then if the one who narrated the addition is known for weak precision, what is narrated by the one known for precision is more appropriate; if both are precise and trustworthy, taking the addition (is preferred).' Al-Amidi said: 'If those who did not narrate the addition reach a number such that forgetfulness of such people about hearing and understanding that addition is unimaginable, then it is obvious that error and oversight affecting one in what he transmitted of the addition is more likely than that affecting the assumed number, so it must be rejected. If they do not reach this limit, then a group of jurists and theologians have agreed on the obligation to accept the addition, contrary to a group of hadith scholars and Ahmad ibn Hanbal in one of two narrations from him.' Ibn al-Hajib and al-Qarafi and others went to this view. Abu al-Khattab al-Kalwadhan said: 'If the transmitter of the addition is a large group, the addition is accepted and the single one may have erred. If the narrator of the addition is one and the narrator of the omission is one, the more famous of them for memory, precision, and trustworthiness is given precedence. If they are equal in all that, then our teacher mentioned from Ahmad two narrations: one that taking the addition is more appropriate, he said in the narration of Ahmad ibn Qasim: the generality of jurists and theologians (hold this); the other: the addition is rejected, which he indicated in the narration of al-Marwadhi and Abu Talib, and with it...'
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of an important usul al-fiqh issue: whether an addition (ziyada) to a hadith by a trustworthy narrator, when other narrators do not mention it, is accepted or rejected. The text opens by stating the positions of various scholars. Some accept the ziyada absolutely because the narrator is trustworthy. Others, notably the majority of Hanafis, reject it absolutely. Imam al-Shafi'i is quoted as arguing that accepting a shadhdha qira'a (irregular Quranic reading) while rejecting a hadith addition is inconsistent, but the response is that the Quran is transmitted by tawatur. The text then presents a nuanced middle position: the ziyada is rejected if the narrator himself first narrated the hadith deficiently and later added it, but accepted from another trustworthy narrator. Ibn Daqiq al-'Id introduces the factor of the transmission session (majlis): if the narrators heard the hadith together, the majority view prevails. Abu Nasr ibn al-Sabbagh refines this with specific scenarios: if two sessions, two reports; if one session, one report, and the addition is judged based on numbers and precision. Al-Amidi adds the criterion of plausibility: if the larger group is so large that it is inconceivable they all missed the addition, then reject it; otherwise accept. The Hanbali position is also cited with two narrations from Ahmad. Overall, the passage illustrates that this issue is resolved through a combination of textual criticism (sanad analysis) and usul principles like tarjih, without a single absolute rule. The Hanafi preferred position (as inferred from 'most Hanafis') leans toward rejection of the ziyada unless supported by a larger number or stronger narrator, reflecting their caution in accepting solitary additions.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An additional word or phrase in a hadith text narrated by one narrator but not by others in the same transmission.
ثقة (thiqah): A narrator known for reliability, memory, and integrity, whose reports are generally accepted.
مجلس (majlis): The session in which the hadith was heard; if narrators heard it in the same session, it is considered one report; if in separate sessions, multiple reports.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Sabbagh, if two narrators transmit a hadith from a single session and one adds a ziyada, and both are equally precise and trustworthy, what is the ruling?
A) The ziyada is rejected.
B) The ziyada is accepted.
C) The narration of the one who did not add is preferred.
D) The hadith is considered two separate reports.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of a ziyada in hadith is not simply based on the narrator's trustworthiness; it involves a careful assessment of the transmission context, including the number of narrators, the nature of the session, and the precision of narrators.

Rule of Suspension (Tawaqquf) When Principles Conflict
Rule of tawaqquf when two usul conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tawaqquf when the principle of non-occurrence and the principle of narrator truthfulness conflict, and identify when tarjih is not possible.

Core Idea
When two equally strong principles conflict, suspend judgment (tawaqquf) — no arbitrary preference.

In usul al-fiqh, scholars often rely on foundational principles (usul) to establish rulings. But what happens when two valid principles point to opposite conclusions? This lesson presents a key Hanafi rule: when the principle of non-occurrence (asl al-'adam) conflicts with the principle of narrator truthfulness (asl sidq al-rawi), and neither can be preferred, the only correct response is to suspend judgment (tawaqquf). This prevents subjective bias and preserves methodological integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting principles
Recognise that the passage sets two usul against each other: the principle of non-occurrence (that an addition did not happen) and the principle of narrator truthfulness (that the narrator is reliable). These are both considered 'asl' (foundational) in Hanafi thought.
Both have the status of a presumptive truth (asl) — neither is inherently stronger.
2
Analyse the reason for conflict
The passage says 'in each of the probabilities there is improbability' (fi kulli wahid min al-ihtimalat bu'dan). This means each principle, while valid, carries some degree of unlikelihood in the specific context. The conflict arises because applying one principle forces rejection of the other.
The improbability (bu'd) does not nullify the principle; it only makes the conflict irresolvable without further evidence.
3
Apply the rule of tawaqquf
When two usul conflict and no tarjih (preference) is possible, the correct approach is wajib al-tawaqquf — suspension of judgment. This is not a failure but a disciplined stance that avoids hasty preference.
Tawaqquf means holding back from a final ruling until further evidence resolves the conflict.
4
Recognise the source and scope
The passage attributes this rule to al-Hindi, indicating it is a recognised position in Hanafi usul. This principle applies to similar cases where two equally authoritative usul point to different conclusions.
This rule is distinct from tarjih (preference) which is used when one side has a clear advantage.
5
Contrast with tawaqquf in other schools
While Hanafis adopt tawaqquf here, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may allow tarjih based on additional criteria such as the number of narrators or strength of memory. Understanding this difference is crucial for comparative fiqh.
The practical outcome may differ: a Shafi'i might accept the addition if the narrator is more reliable, while a Hanafi would suspend.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوقف؛ لأن في كُلّ واحد من الاحتمالات بعداً والأصل وإن كان عدم الصدور، لكن الأصل أيضاً صدق الرَّاوِي وَإِذَا تعارضا وجب التوقف. حكاه الهندي.
Suspension, because in each of the probabilities there is improbability; and although the original principle is non-occurrence, yet the original principle is also the truthfulness of the narrator, and when they conflict, suspension is obligatory. Al-Hindi reported it.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage establishes the rule of tawaqquf (suspension) when there is conflict between two usul (principles): the principle of non-existence (i.e., that the addition did not occur) and the principle of the narrator's truthfulness. Since both are valid principles but point to opposite conclusions, and neither clearly outweighs the other, the scholar must suspend judgment. This is a key usul principle for handling undecidable conflicts in hadith transmission. Al-Hindi reported this as a recognized approach.

Key Terms
الوقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment when evidence is conflicting and no preference can be established.
الأصل (asl): A foundational principle that is presumed true unless evidence overrides it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is suspension (tawaqquf) required when the principle of non-occurrence and the principle of narrator truthfulness conflict?
A) Because the narrator is always to be believed.
B) Because non-occurrence is stronger.
C) Because both principles have improbability and conflict, so no preference can be made.
D) Because al-Hindi reported it as such.

Key Takeaway
When two valid usul conflict without clear preference, suspension (tawaqquf) is obligatory in Hanafi usul.

Ziyada from a Trustworthy Narrator: The Usul vs. Hadith Schism
Ruling on ziyada from a thiqah narrator: occasional vs. frequent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between usul scholars and hadith scholars regarding ziyada from a thiqah narrator known for frequent additions, and identify the basis for each view.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's occasional addition is accepted; frequent additions trigger a dispute: usul accept, hadith reject due to suspicion.

This passage first establishes that an occasional addition (shudhudh) from a trustworthy narrator is accepted, citing Malik's report about zakat al-fitr. The real controversy arises when the narrator is known for many additions in the same session without clear differentiation. Two scholarly camps differ: usul scholars (fuqaha') accept based on general reliability, while hadith scholars (muhaddithun) reject due to suspicion (tuhma) of error or fabrication. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting evidences in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) the narrator is thiqah and rarely adds (shudhudh), and (2) the narrator is thiqah but known for frequent additions in a single session. Recognize that the first is unanimously accepted, the second is disputed.
The example of Malik's narration shows the first scenario.
2
State the agreed ruling
When the addition is occasional, it is accepted. Confirm this with the text: the narrator is trustworthy and not known for additions, and the addition occurs 'ala tariq al-shudhudh.
Shudhudh here means anomalous but not necessarily rejected.
3
Identify the point of disagreement
When the narrator is known for many additions with no distinction in hearing (e.g., same session, no indication of separate hearings), the scholars differed. Pinpoint that the dispute hinges on frequency.
The condition 'ittihad al-majlis' (single session) is key.
4
Understand the usul scholars' argument
Usul scholars accept the addition because the narrator remains thiqah; reliability is not negated by frequency. They prioritize the narrator's general trustworthiness over the possibility of error.
This is the dominant Hanafi position.
5
Understand the hadith scholars' argument
Hadith scholars reject the addition due to tuhma (suspicion). Frequency of anomaly weakens confidence; they fear the narrator may have added from memory or confusion. They require additional corroboration.
Tuhma does not imply lie, but potential mistake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٠٩ إذَا كَانَ راوي الزيادة ثِقَة وَلَمْ يشتهر بنقل الزيادة ولكن كَانَ ذَلِكَ مِنْهُ عَلَى طريق الشذوذ قبلت كرواية مَالِك من المُسْلِمِينَ في صدقة الفطر، وإن اشتهر بكثرة الزيادات مَعَ اتحاد المجلس وَلَمْ يَكُنْ هناك امتياز بسماع فاختلفوا فيه، فمذهب الأصوليين قبول زيادته، ومذهب المُحَدِّثِينَ ردها للتهمة. قَالَهُ أَبُو الحَسَن الأبياري.
9. If the narrator of the addition is trustworthy and not known for conveying additions, but that occurs from him in an anomalous way, it is accepted, like the narration of Malik from 'the Muslims' regarding charity of fitr. But if he is known for many additions while the session is the same and there is no distinction in hearing, then they differed. The view of the usul scholars is acceptance of his addition, and the view of the hadith scholars is rejection due to suspicion. Abu al-Hasan al-Abyari stated it.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between usul scholars (fuqaha') and hadith scholars (muhaddithun) regarding a narrator known for frequent additions. If the narrator is trustworthy and rarely adds (shudhudh), the addition is accepted, exemplifed by Malik's narration about zakat al-fitr. However, if the narrator is known for many additions in one session without clear distinction, usul scholars accept the addition, while hadith scholars reject it due to possible tampering. This highlights the different methodologies: usul scholars prioritize general reliability, while hadith scholars are more cautious about frequency of anomalies.

Key Terms
شذوذ (shudhudh): An anomalous narration where a reliable narrator contradicts more reliable narrators; here it means occasional, rare addition.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion that the narrator may have fabricated or erred due to frequent anomalous narrations.
أصوليون (usuliyyun): Scholars of usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence).
محدثون (muhaddithun): Hadith scholars who specialize in criticism of narrators and texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the view of hadith scholars (muhaddithin) regarding a narrator known for frequent additions in the same session?
A) They accept the addition because the narrator is trustworthy.
B) They reject the addition due to suspicion.
C) They suspend judgment.
D) They accept only if the addition changes the i'rab.

Key Takeaway
A trustworthy narrator's occasional addition is accepted; but when the narrator is known for frequent additions in a single session, usul scholars accept while hadith scholars reject due to suspicion, reflecting a methodological difference in weighing reliability versus caution.

Conditions for Accepting Ziyada: Scholarly Disagreements
List of conditions from several scholars for accepting ziyada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the conditions set by Qadi Abd al-Wahhab, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Khatib, and al-Sayrafi for accepting a ziyada from a solitary narrator, and evaluate which condition is strictest.

Core Idea
Scholars differ: from mere trustworthiness to proficiency—on when a solitary ziyada is accepted.

The acceptance of an addition (ziyada) from a solitary narrator is a debated topic in hadith and usul al-fiqh. Different scholars set varying thresholds: some require only trustworthiness, others demand memorization and proficiency. This passage presents the views of four scholars, revealing a spectrum from leniency to strictness. Understanding these conditions helps us evaluate the strength of hadith-based rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Understand that the dispute is about accepting a ziyada (addition) narrated by a single narrator when other narrators do not have that addition.
A ziyada can change the ruling derived from a hadith.
2
List each scholar's condition
Extract the condition from each scholar: Qadi Abd al-Wahhab reports from Malik and Abu Farj: thiqah dabit; Ibn Khuzaymah: hafiz and knowledgeable; al-Khatib: hafiz and mutqin; al-Sayrafi: generally acceptable for solitary narrations.
Note the Arabic terms: ثقة ضابط, حافظ, متقن.
3
Compare the conditions
Rank the conditions from most lenient (al-Sayrafi) to strictest (al-Khatib). Identify which scholars require more than just basic reliability.
Al-Sayrafi’s condition is the most lenient; al-Khatib’s is the most demanding.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider how the condition affects the acceptance of a ziyada. For example, under al-Khatib’s condition, many narrators would be rejected; under al-Sayrafi’s, most reliable narrators’ additions are accepted.
This determines the number of prophetic practices that enter the fiqh.
5
Relate to usul al-fiqh
Understand that these conditions are part of the methodology for verifying hadith. Different usul principles lead to different thresholds for accepting narrations, which impacts the derivation of legal rulings.
This ikhtilaf is a mercy; it enriches the legal tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ الْقَاضِي عَبْد الوهاب المالكي: «إذا انفرد بغض رواة الحديث بزيادة وخالفهم بقية الرواة، فعن مالك وأبي فرج من أصحابنا تقبل إن كَانَ ثِقَة ضابطاً . وَقِيلَ: إنَّها تقبل إذَا كَانَ راويها حافظاً عالماً بالأخبار، فإذا لَمْ يَكُنْ يلحق من لَمْ يَرْوِ الزيادة بالحفظ لَمْ تقبل وَهُوَ قَوْل ابن خزيمة. واشترط الْخَطِيْب: أن يَكُون راوي الزيادة حافظاً متقناً، وَقَالَ الصَّيْرَفِي: «إن كُلّ من لَوْ انفرد بحديث يقبل، فإن زيادته مقبولة وإن خالف الحفاظ».
Qadi Abd al-Wahhab al-Maliki said: 'If some of the narrators of a hadith are alone with an addition and the rest of the narrators contradict them, then according to Malik and Abu Farj from our companions, it is accepted if he is trustworthy and precise. And it is said: it is accepted if its narrator is a memorizer and knowledgeable of reports; if he is not, he cannot be compared to the one who did not narrate the addition in terms of memory, and it is not accepted. This is the view of Ibn Khuzaymah. Al-Khatib stipulated that the narrator of the addition be a memorizer and proficient. And al-Sayrafi said: 'Anyone who, if he alone narrated a hadith, would have his narration accepted, then his addition is accepted even if he contradicts the memorizers.'
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage surveys the conditions set by different scholars for accepting a ziyada (addition) from a narrator who is alone in that addition. Qadi Abd al-Wahhab reports from Malik and Abu Farj that the narrator must be trustworthy (thiqah) and precise (dabit). Ibn Khuzaymah adds the condition of being a memorizer (hafiz) and knowledgeable in hadith reports. Al-Khatib requires both memory and proficiency (mutqin). Al-Sayrafi takes the most lenient position: if the narrator is generally acceptable for solitary narrations, his addition is accepted even if it contradicts the majority of memorizers. This shows a spectrum from strict to lenient conditions.

Key Terms
ثقة ضابط (thiqah dabit): A reliable narrator who is precise in transmission, meeting conditions for acceptance.
حافظ (hafiz): A hadith memorizer with extensive knowledge of narrations and chains.
متقن (mutqin): Proficient and precise in narration, with no known errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) If the narrator's solitary narrations are generally accepted, his addition is accepted even if he contradicts memorizers.
D) Only if the addition adds a new legal ruling.

Key Takeaway
Scholars set varying conditions for accepting a ziyada, from trustworthiness to proficiency, reflecting different methodological priorities in preserving the sunnah.

Ibn Hibban's Condition: Narrator Must Be Predominantly Faqih for Ziyada
Ibn Hibban's condition that narrator must be primarily a faqih to accept ziyada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate Ibn Hibban's condition for accepting ziyada and contrast it with the standard Hanafi acceptance of trustworthy narrators.

Core Idea
Ibn Hibban: Only accept ziyada from a faqih who understands meaning, not just a muhaddith.

This lesson explores a unique position by Ibn Hibban regarding the acceptance of added words in hadith. He argues that juristic understanding, not just accuracy in transmission, is required for such additions. The Hanafi school, while generally accepting sound narrators, also values understanding in certain contexts. We will dissect his rationale and compare it to mainstream usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
State Ibn Hibban's requirement for accepting additions (ziyada) in narrations.
He requires the narrator to be predominantly a faqih.
2
Understand the Rationale
Explain why Ibn Hibban prioritizes fiqh over hadith memorization for additions.
He argues that a faqih understands the meaning and can discern whether an addition distorts the original.
3
Contrast with General Hanafi Approach
Compare Ibn Hibban's view with the general Hanafi principle of accepting ziyada from trustworthy narrators regardless of specialization.
The Hanafi school accepts ziyada from any trustworthy narrator (thiqah), as long as it is not contradicted by stronger evidence.

قَالَ ابْن حِبَّان: و أما زيادة الألفاظ في الروايات فإنا لا نقبل شيئاً منها إلا عمّن كَانَ الغالب عَلَيْهِ الفقه حَتَّى يعلم أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْوِي الشيء ويعلمه حَتَّى لا يشك فِيهِ أَنَّهُ أزاله عن سننه أو غيره عن معناه أم لا؛ لأن أصحاب الحَدِيث الغالب عَلَيْهِمْ حفظ الأسامي والأسانيد دُونَ المتون، والفُقَهَاء الغالب عَلَيْهِمْ

Because hadith scholars are predominantly concerned with memorizing names and chains, not texts, while jurists are predominantly...'

Commentary
Ibn Hibban introduces a unique criterion: the narrator of a ziyada (addition) must be predominantly a faqih (jurist), not just a muhaddith (hadith scholar). His reasoning is that jurists understand the meaning and context of the hadith, so they are less likely to change or distort it. Hadith scholars, on the other hand, often focus on names and chains (isnad) rather than understanding the text (matn). Therefore, an addition from a pure muhaddith is suspect. This passage is cut off but the gist is clear: Ibn Hibban prioritizes juristic knowledge for accepting additions.

Key Terms
فقه (fiqh): Deep understanding of Islamic law and legal implications of texts.
أصحاب الحديث (ashab al-hadith): Hadith scholars who focus on memorizing chains of transmission.

Acceptance of Ziyada from a Trustworthy Narrator
Discussion of the ruling on accepting additions in hadith narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that additions from trustworthy narrators are evaluated case-by-case using contextual indications (qara'in), and distinguish this from the opposing view of absolute acceptance.

Core Idea
No universal rule: each addition from a thiqah is judged individually by hadith critics.

In this passage, we explore a fundamental usul principle: how should we treat an addition (ziyada) in a hadith made by a trustworthy narrator (thiqah)? Contrary to a common misconception, the early hadith critics—and the Hanafi school following them—did not apply a blanket acceptance. Instead, they examined each addition in light of contextual evidence (qara'in). This lesson unpacks the nuanced methodology of the critics and the scholarly dispute with those who argued for absolute acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The key question: when a reliable narrator adds something to a hadith that other trustworthy narrators do not report, should this addition be automatically accepted?
This is a classic usul debate about ziyadat al-thiqah.
2
Distinguish the two positions
One position, advocated by al-Khatib al-Baghdadi, holds that any addition from a just, precise narrator is accepted categorically. The other, supported by the majority of hadith critics (including the Hanafi school), holds that each addition must be evaluated individually using qara'in.
The majority view relies on the actual practice of critics like Bukhari and Abu Hatim.
3
Examine the role of qara'in
According to Ibn Hajar and al-'Ala'i, the acceptance or rejection of an addition depends on contextual indications: whether the addition contradicts stronger evidence, whether it stands as an independent report, or whether it appears to be inserted (mudraj) from another source.
No single rule covers all cases; preponderance (tarjih) factors are numerous and case-specific.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi usul aligns with the critical method: the addition is scrutinized for error, confusion, or forgetfulness, and only accepted after assurance of the narrator's safety from such defects. The decisive factor is the critic's expertise, not a mechanical rule.
Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi: 'The proof is memory, understanding, and knowledge, nothing else.'
5
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah)
The difference matters: under al-Khatib's view, many mursal or interrupted hadith with a thiqah's addition might be accepted; under the majority view, such additions are often rejected unless supported by other evidence.
This affects how we derive rulings from hadith in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
تصرفهم من الزيادة قبولاً ورداً الترجيح بالنسبة إلى ما يقوى عِنْدَ الواحد مِنْهُمْ في كُلّ حَدِيث، وَلاً يحكمون في المسألة بحكم كلي يعم جميع الأحاديث). هَذَا العرض يتبين أن كثيراً من الفُقَهَاء والأصوليين وفريقاً من المُحَدِّثِينَ قَدْ من أطلقوا القَوْل بقبول زيادة الثّقة وجنحوا لِذلِكَ في كَثِير من الأحيان، والمرجوع إليه في مثل هذِهِ الأمور المُحَدِّثُونَ لا غيرهم، فَقَدْ كَانَ المُحَدِّثُونَ يحكمون عَلَى كُلّ رِوَايَة بما يناسبها، وهم المعوّل عَلَيْهِمْ في مَعْرِفَة أحكام زيادة الثّقة، فيجب الرجوع إليهم وحدهم لكونها من ضمن تخصصاتهم النقدية، وليست هي من تخصصات غيرهم. ونظر المُحَدِّثِيْنَ يختلف في الحكم على الأحاديث؛ إذ إن زيادة النّقة عندهم مِنْهَا ما هُوَ مقبول، ومنها ما هُوَ مردود تبعاً للقرائن المحيطة بها، والقرائن هِيَ الَّتِي تجعل الحكم مختلفاً من حديث لآخر فمن القرائن ما يدل عَلَى أن الزيادة تكون أحياناً مدرجة في الحَدِيث، أو أَنَّهَا من قَوْل أحد رُوَاة الإسناد أو من حَدِيث آخر. قَالَ الحَافِظ ابن حجر: «مَا تفرد بَعْض الرُّوَاة بزيادة فِيهِ دُونَ من هُوَ أكثر عدداً أو أضبط مِمَّنْ لَمْ يذكرها، فهذا يؤثر التعليل بِهِ إلا إن كَانَتْ الزيادة منافية بِحَيْثُ يتعذر الجمع. أما إن كَانَتِ الزيادة لا منافاة فِيهَا بِحَيْثُ تَكون كالحديث المستقل فلا، اللَّهُمَّ إلا إن وضح بالدلائل القوية أن تلك الزيادة مدرجة في المثن من كلام بَعْض رواته، فما كَانَ القِسْم فَهُوَ مؤثر» (٢). وربما تكون الزيادة غَيْر صَحِيحَة لأمر آخر رُبَّمَا لا يفصح عَنْهُ المحدّث كَمَا لا يستطيع أن يفصح الجوهري عن زيف الزائف (۳) وربما قبل المُحَدِّثُوْنَ الزيادة الواقعة في بعض المتون أو الأسانيد لقرائن تخص ذَلِكَ ومرجحات خَاصَّة وَهِي كثيرة، قَالَ العلائي: «ووجوه الترجيح كثيرة لا تنحصر، وَلا ضابط لَهَا بالنسبة إلى جَمِيع الأحاديث، بَلْ كُلّ حَدِيث يقوم به ترجيح خاص. وإنما ينهض بِذَلِكَ الممارس الفطن الذي أكثر من الطرق والروايات؛ ولهذا لم يحكم المتقدمون في هَذَا المقام بحكم كلي يشمل القاعدة، بَلْ يختلف نظرهم بحسب يقوم عندهم في كُلّ حَدِيث بمفرده»(4). وَقَدْ توهم من ظن أنَّ النقاد موقفهم واحد في كُلّ الزيادات؛ إذ إن النقاد إذا كانوا قد نصوا في بَعْض المناسبات عَلَى قبول زيادة النّقة أو الأوثق، بحيث يخيل إلى القارئ المتعجل أن موقفهم في ذَلِكَ هُوَ القبول المطلق، فَهُوَ تخيل غَيْر صَحِيح، إِذْ إِن عمل النقاد النقدي المتمثل في رد الزيادة مرة وقبولها أخرى بغض النظر عن حال الرَّاوِي الثّقة أو الأوثق يَكُون ذَلِكَ كافياً للتفسير بأن ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ حكماً مطرداً مِنْهُمْ، وإنما قبلوا في حال الرَّاوِي الثَّقَة الَّذِي زاد في الحَدِيث زيادة بَعْدَ تأكدهم من سلامته من جَمِيع الملابسات الدالة عَلَى احتمال الخطأ والوهم أو النسيان، ويؤكد هَذَا المَعْنَى الحَاكِم النيسابوري قائلاً: «الحجة فيه عندنا الحفظ والفهم والمَعْرِفَة لا غَيْر » (۱) . لكن الخطيب البغدادي - فِيمَا أعلم - هُوَ أول المُحَدِّثِينَ في النقل عن الْجُمْهُورِ بقبول زيادة الثّقة ورجح ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ: والَّذِي نختاره من هذه الأقوال: أن الزيادة الواردة مقبولة عَلَى كُلّ حال معمول بِهَا إذَا كَانَ راويها عدلاً ومتقناً ضابطاً (٢).
وَقَد ناقشه ابن رجب الحنبلي فِيْمَا استدل بِهِ فَقَالَ: (وذكر في الكفاية حكاية عن البُخَارِيّ : أَنَّهُ سُئل عن حَدِيث أبي إسحاق في النكاح بلا ولى (٤) قَالَ: الزيادة من
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. Their dealing with addition, acceptance and rejection, is preference relative to what is strong with each one of them in every hadith, and they do not rule on the issue with a universal ruling that covers all hadith. This presentation makes clear that many jurists and usul scholars and a group of hadith scholars have absolutely stated the acceptance of the addition of the trustworthy and inclined to that frequently. But the reference in such matters is the hadith scholars, not others. For the hadith scholars used to judge every narration according to what suits it, and they are the ones relied upon in knowing the rulings on the addition of the trustworthy. So it is obligatory to refer to them alone because it is part of their critical specialization, and it is not the specialization of others. And the view of the hadith scholars differs in the ruling on hadith; for indeed, the addition of the trustworthy according to them includes what is accepted and what is rejected depending on the surrounding indications. And the indications are what make the ruling differ from one hadith to another. Among the indications are that the addition is sometimes inserted into the hadith, or that it is from the statement of one of the narrators of the chain or from another hadith. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'What some narrators uniquely add without those who are more numerous or more precise who did not mention it, this affects its being defective unless the addition is contradictory such that reconciliation is impossible. As for if the addition is not contradictory such that it is like an independent hadith, then no, unless it is clarified by strong proofs that that addition is inserted into the text from the speech of some of its narrators, then whatever is the division is effective.' And perhaps the addition is not authentic for another reason that the hadith scholar may not disclose, just as the jeweler cannot disclose the falsity of the counterfeit. And perhaps the hadith scholars accept the addition occurring in some texts or chains due to specific indications and particular preponderances, which are numerous. Al-'Ala'i said: 'The aspects of preponderance are numerous and not limited, and there is no control for them with respect to all hadith. Rather, every hadith has a particular preponderance that arises. Only the experienced, intelligent practitioner who has many paths and narrations can accomplish that. For this reason, the early scholars did not rule in this context with a universal ruling encompassing the principle; rather their view differs according to what arises with them in every hadith individually.' And indeed, some have deluded themselves into thinking that the critics have a single position on all additions. For if the critics have stated on some occasions the acceptance of the addition of the trustworthy or the more reliable, such that it might appear to the hasty reader that their position on that is absolute acceptance, that is an incorrect delusion. For indeed, the critical work of the critics, consisting of rejecting the addition sometimes and accepting it at other times regardless of the state of the trustworthy or more reliable narrator, is sufficient to explain that this is not a consistent ruling from them. Rather, they only accepted in the case of the trustworthy narrator who added to the hadith after they were assured of his safety from all circumstances indicating the possibility of error, confusion, or forgetfulness. Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi confirms this meaning, saying: 'The proof for us is memory, understanding, and knowledge, nothing else.' But al-Khatib al-Baghdadi - as far as I know - is the first of the hadith scholars to transmit from the majority the acceptance of the addition of the trustworthy and he preferred that, saying: 'What I choose from these statements is that the addition that comes is accepted in all cases and acted upon if its narrator is just, precise, and reliable.' Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali discussed what he (al-Khatib) used as evidence, saying: 'He mentioned in al-Kifayah a report from al-Bukhari that he was asked about the hadith of Abu Ishaq on marriage without a guardian. He said: The addition is from
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the usul principle of accepting (or rejecting) an addition (ziyada) made by a trustworthy narrator (thiqah) in a hadith. The author explains that contrary to the impression given by some jurists and usul scholars, hadith critics do not apply a blanket rule. Instead, each addition is judged individually based on contextual indicators (qara'in). The passage cites several key authorities: Ibn Hajar distinguishes between additions that contradict—making reconciliation impossible (which affect the hadith's authenticity)—and those that are like independent reports (which are generally acceptable unless proven inserted). Al-'Ala'i emphasizes that preponderance (tarjih) factors are numerous and case-specific, hence early scholars avoided a universal rule. The author then refutes the misconception that critics always accept additions from trustworthy narrators, noting that criticism includes rejection when error is suspected. Al-Hakim al-Naysaburi is quoted to show that the deciding factor is the critic's knowledge and memory, not a mechanical rule. Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi is presented as an exception, arguing for absolute acceptance of additions from reliable narrators. However, Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali critiques al-Khatib's reliance on a report from al-Bukhari regarding the hadith of Abu Ishaq on marriage without a guardian, implying that the addition is not universally accepted. The passage thus underscores that the Hanafi usul position aligns with the majority of hadith scholars: there is no categorical acceptance or rejection; rather, the addition is evaluated in light of all available evidence.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition to the matn or sanad of a hadith made by a narrator beyond what other narrators report.
ثقة (thiqah): A narrator who is reliable, just, and precise in transmission.
قرائن (qara'in): Indications or contextual evidence that help determine whether an addition is acceptable or not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of hadith scholars as described in the passage, what is the ruling on an addition (ziyada) made by a trustworthy narrator?
A) It is always accepted if the narrator is thiqah.
B) It is always rejected unless the narrator is the most reliable.
C) It is evaluated individually based on contextual indications (qara'in).
D) It is accepted only if the narrator is both thiqah and an imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle: no blanket acceptance of ziyadat al-thiqah; each addition must be critically evaluated using contextual evidence (qara'in).

Accepting the Addition of a Trustworthy Narrator: The Marriage Guardian Hadith
Analyzing the principle of ziyadat al-thiqah through the disputed hadith on marriage guardian

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the acceptance of a trustworthy narrator's addition (ziyadat al-thiqah) by applying the Hanafi usul principle and analyzing the chain evidence for the marriage guardian hadith.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's addition is not automatically accepted; it must pass scrutiny against error and contradiction.

This lesson explores the nuanced principle of ziyadat al-thiqah through the case of the marriage guardian hadith. While some scholars advocate absolute acceptance, the critical practice of muhaddithin shows a case-by-case approach. We will examine the debate and the chain analysis that supports the Hanafi requirement of a guardian.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of ziyadat al-thiqah
Understand what is meant by the addition of a trustworthy narrator and how al-Khatib al-Baghdadi argued for absolute acceptance.
Al-Khatib's condition: narrator must be 'adl and mutqin.
2
Analyze Ibn Rajab's critique
Examine the objection based on al-Bukhari's hesitation and the claim that addition is not automatically accepted.
Ibn Rajab quotes al-Bukhari saying 'the addition is from the memory of so-and-so'.
3
Examine the chain analysis of the hadith
The hadith 'لا نكاح إلا بولي' is narrated in both mursal (by Shu'bah and Sufyan) and musnad forms. Count the narrators and assess strength.
The author lists numerous narrators for the musnad version.
4
Apply the principle to determine preponderance
Use the chain evidence: the musnad version has more and stronger narrators, outweighing the mursal.
The author concludes that the musnad is preponderant (rajih).
5
Derive the ruling from the hadith
The musnad hadith establishes that a guardian is a necessary condition for a valid marriage, supporting the Hanafi position.
This hadith is used as a primary dalil in Hanafi fiqh.

قَدْ نصوا في بَعْض المناسبات عَلَى قبول زيادة النّقة أو الأوثق، بحيث يخيل إلى القارئ المتعجل أن موقفهم في ذَلِكَ هُوَ القبول المطلق، فَهُوَ تخيل غَيْر صَحِيح، إِذْ إِن عمل النقاد النقدي المتمثل في رد الزيادة مرة وقبولها أخرى بغض النظر عن حال الرَّاوِي الثّقة أو الأوثق يَكُون ذَلِكَ كافياً للتفسير بأن ذَلِكَ لَيْسَ حكماً مطرداً مِنْهُمْ، وإنما قبلوا في حال الرَّاوِي الثَّقَة الَّذِي زاد في الحَدِيث زيادة بَعْدَ تأكدهم من سلامته من جَمِيع الملابسات الدالة عَلَى احتمال الخطأ والوهم أو النسيان، ويؤكد هَذَا المَعْنَى الحَاكِم النيسابوري قائلاً: «الحجة فيه عندنا الحفظ والفهم والمَعْرِفَة لا غَيْر » (۱) . لكن الخطيب البغدادي - فِيمَا أعلم - هُوَ أول المُحَدِّثِينَ في النقل عن الْجُمْهُورِ بقبول زيادة الثّقة ورجح ذَلِكَ فَقَالَ: والَّذِي نختاره من هذه الأقوال: أن الزيادة الواردة مقبولة عَلَى كُلّ حال معمول بِهَا إذَا كَانَ راويها عدلاً ومتقناً ضابطاً (٢).

(۲) الكفاية (٥٩٧ ت، ٤٢٥هـ).
(۳)
(۳) هُوَ عَمْرو بن عبيد ويقال: عَمْرو بن عَبْد الله بن عَلِي، ويقال: عَمْرو بن عبد الله بن أبي شعيرة الهمداني، أبو إسحاق السبيعي الكوفي : ثقة مكثر عابد اختلط بأخرة، توفي سنة (۱۲۹) هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (١٢٦ هـ) وَقِيْلَ غَيْر ذَلِكَ.
النعمان

تهذيب الكمال ۱۳۱/٥ (٤۹۸۹) ، والكاشف (۸۲/۲ (٤١٨٥) ، والتقريب (٥٠٦٥). (٤) هُوَ حَدِيث أبي إسحاق السَّبِيعِي عن أبي بردة عن أبيه أنّ رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لا نكاح إلا بولي». وهذا الحديث اختلف في وصله وإرساله والراجح وصله – كما يأتي أولاً : تفرّد بإرساله شعبة وسفيان الثوري، واختلف عليهما فيه: فقد رواه عن شعبة موصولاً: بن عبد السلام عند الحاكم في المستدرك ٢ / ١٦٩ ، عنه، وعن سفيان الثوري مقرونين، والبيهقي في الكبرى ۷ / ۱۰۹ ، ويزيد بن زريع عند البزار في مسنده ٩٤/٢، والدارقطني في سننه ۲۲٠/٣، والبيهقي في الكبرى ۷ / ۱۰۹ ومالك بن سليمان عند الخطيب البغدادي في تاريخ بغداد ٢١٤/٢ عنه وعن إسرائيل، وكذلك رواه عن شعبة موصولاً: محمد بن موسى الحرشي، ومحمد بن حصين كما ذكر الدارقطني في العلل ٧ / ٢٠٦، فهؤلاء خمستهم النعمان بن عبد السلام ويزيد بن زريع ومالك بن سليمان ومحمد بن موسى، ومحمد بن
حصين) رووه عن شعبة، عن أبي إسحاق، عن أبي بردة عن أبي موسى، مرفوعاً.
