How a Single Word Changed the Ruling: Tayammum Dispute
Usul dispute over a hadith addition on tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the substance for tayammum by analyzing the textual addition in the hadith of Hudhayfa and applying the usul principle of ziyadat al-thiqa.

Core Idea
A solitary addition in a hadith is rejected if it contradicts a stronger general text; thus, tayammum remains valid on all earth.

This lesson explores how a single word — 'turbatuha' (its dust) — in a hadith narrated by Abu Malik from Hudhayfa became a point of divergence between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. By examining the usul principle of accepting or rejecting isolated additions (ziyadat al-thiqa), we see how the same source can generate different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed text
Locate the hadith addition 'turbatuha' and understand why it matters. Compare the version with and without this word.
The addition appears only in the narration of Abu Malik from Rib'i from Hudhayfa.
2
Categorize the textual element
Classify the addition as a ziyadat thiqa (addition by a reliable narrator) or a shadh (irregular) addition. Note that other narrators did not include it.
In Hanafi usul, a solitary addition is considered zanni al-thubut.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule
The Hanafi school holds that a general (amm) Quranic text is qat'i and cannot be restricted by a zanni addition unless proven with certainty. Since the addition is solitary and contradicts the general command, it is rejected.
The general command is Quran 5:6: 'فَامْسَحُوا بِوُجُوهِكُمْ وَأَيْدِيكُمْ مِنْهُ'.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
From the general command, tayammum is valid with any sa'id (earth), including sand, stones, and gypsum.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and the majority of the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i reading
The Shafi'i school accepts the addition as authentic and restricts tayammum to pure dust (turab). This shows the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
The difference affects millions of Muslims in regions where water is scarce.

Source Text

Chapter Three: Disagreement in Chain and Text. It resembles the first division in that what the group narrates is general and what the individual narrates with an addition is specific, and therein is a difference in attribute and a type of divergence by which the ruling differs. It also resembles the second division in that there is no contradiction between them. This is from al-Hafiz Ibn al-Salah a precise and deep insight, because there is no addition in the hadith mentioned by a narrator that the rest of the narrators did not mention from the same pivot (narrator at the center) and unity of source. For Abu Malik alone narrated the entire hadith from Rib‘i, and Rib‘i alone narrated it from Hudhayfa, except that in this hadith there is an addition beyond what was mentioned in other hadiths from other Companions. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar commented on Ibn al-Salah's work, saying: 'This example is also not correct; because Abu Malik alone narrated the entire hadith from Rib‘i ibn Hirash as he alone narrated its entirety from Rib‘i from Hudhayfa. If he means that the word "turbatuha" (its dust) is an addition in this hadith beyond the other hadiths in general, then it is refuted because it is also in the hadith of 'Ali... In any case, whatever Ibn al-Salah intended, this hadith and its addition have an effect in Islamic jurisprudence. The jurists differed on what suffices for tayammum into two opinions: 1. It is not valid except with dust that has dust that sticks to the hand. This is the view of Ibn 'Abbas, al-Shafi‘i, Ahmad, Ishaq, Abu Yusuf, Ibn al-Mundhir, Dawud, and the Zaydiyya. It is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ishaq the condition that the soil be sweet (non-saline). 2. Tayammum is valid with everything that is of the type of earth. This is the view of Hammad ibn Sulayman, Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Yahya ibn Sa‘id. And Malik said: it is valid with everything that is on the surface of the earth. And Sufyan al-Thawri said: If there is dust on your garment, saddle, or pack-saddle, or on a tree, then perform tayammum with it. It is valid even with snow. This is the view of Malik, al-Awza‘i, and al-Thawri. And in a narration from Malik, it is valid with everything connected to the earth from vegetation. 4. Tayammum is valid with sand: this is a narration from al-Shafi‘i, Abu Yusuf, Ahmad, al-Awza‘i, and Abu Thawr. 5. The school of Ibn Hazm: earth is two types: soil and non-soil. As for soil, tayammum with it is permissible if it is in its place from the earth. As for other than soil, such as pebbles or rock...
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of how differences in hadith chains and texts (as an example of usul al-fiqh) lead to differences in fiqh rulings. The author first presents Ibn al-Salah's classification of narrational differences, then Ibn Hajar's critique regarding the specific hadith on tayammum narrated by Abu Malik from Rib‘i from Hudhayfa. The key point is that the addition of the word 'turbatuha' (its dust) in this hadith affects the ruling. The passage then lists the famous juristic positions on what suffices for tayammum. The first position (strict) limits tayammum to pure dust that leaves a residue, held by Shafi‘i, Ahmad, and early Abu Yusuf. The second (expansive) allows any earth-like substance, held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Malik allows anything on the earth's surface, including snow and vegetation in one narration. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that tayammum is valid with anything from the earth, including sand and stones, based on the general command in the Quran (5:6) 'so wipe your faces and hands with it' where 'it' refers to the earth (sa‘id). This is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Ritual purification with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.
التربة (al-turbah): Dust or soil, specifically the substance used for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, the addition 'turbatuha' in the hadith of Hudhayfa is:
A) Accepted as authentic and binding.
B) Rejected because it contradicts the general Quranic command.
C) Considered equivalent to the Quran.
D) Used to restrict tayammum to dust.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's rejection of the solitary addition 'turbatuha' in the tayammum hadith preserves the general ruling that tayammum is valid on any earth, demonstrating the priority of qat'i over zanni evidence.

Accepting an Increase (Ziyada) in a Hadith: The Case of Raising Hands in Prayer
An example of an acceptable increase (ziyada) in a hadith due to multiple narrators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a ziyada from a reliable narrator is accepted when supported by multiple chains.

Core Idea
A ziyada in a hadith is accepted when multiple reliable chains confirm it, even if other narrations omit it.

This lesson examines a famous hadith on raising hands in prayer, where an additional wording (raising hands after two rak'ahs) is narrated through multiple chains. We will see how Hanafi usul treats such an increase (ziyada) and why it is considered acceptable when supported by multiple reliable narrators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and the ziyada
Read the source passage and locate the extra wording: the mention of raising hands when standing after two rak'ahs. This is the ziyada in question.
The ziyada is the phrase 'وَإِذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه'.
2
Map the chains of transmission
Note the three paths from Abd al-A'la: via 'Ayyash, Nasr ibn Ali, and Isma'il ibn Bishr. All three narrate the same version including the ziyada.
These chains are documented by Bukhari, Abu Dawud, al-Bayhaqi, etc.
3
Understand the opposition
The passage mentions two types of opposition: some narrations do not attribute the hadith to the Prophet (mawquf), and some omit the fourth raising. Identify these as opposing versions.
Opposition (mukhalafah) does not automatically reject the ziyada.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle of ziyada
Since multiple reliable narrators (the three) agree on the increase, it is accepted over the opposing versions. In Hanafi usul, a ziyada from a trustworthy narrator is accepted if corroborated by others.
This is the principle: ziyada al-thiqah maqbula idha ta'addadat al-turuq.
5
Derive the usul conclusion
The ziyada is accepted as part of the hadith, establishing the sunnah of raising hands at four points. This conclusion is based on the strength of multiple chains.
The ruling is zanni al-thubut but operative in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رَوَى عَبْد الأعلى عن عبيد الله بن عُمَر عن نافع أَن عَبْد الله بن عُمَر كَانَ إذا دخل في الصَّلاة كبر ورفع يديه، وإذا ركع رفع يديه، وَإِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَنْ حمده رفع يديه، وَإِذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه، رفع ذَلِكَ ابن عُمَر إلى النَّبي . هكذا رَواهُ الإِمَامِ البُخَارِيّ وابن حزم من طريق عياش، وأبو داؤد، والبيهقي من طريق نصر بن عَلِيّ، والبيهقي، والبيهقي، والبغوي من طريق إسماعيل بن بشر بن مَنْصُوْر؛ ثلاثتهم ( عياش، ونصر بن علي، وإسماعيل بن بشر) رووه عن عبد الأعلى من هَذَا الوجه. وَقَدْ خولف عَبْد الأعلى في هَذَا الحَدِيث مرتين: خولف في رفعه وخولف بذكر
Abd al-A'la narrated from Ubaydullah ibn Umar from Nafi' that Abdullah ibn Umar used to, when he entered prayer, say the takbir and raise his hands; when he bowed, he raised his hands; when he said 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', he raised his hands; when he stood up from the two rak'ahs, he raised his hands; he raised that (narrated it as marfu') to the Prophet (peace be upon him). Thus it was narrated by Imam al-Bukhari and Ibn Hazm via the path of 'Ayyash; by Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi via the path of Nasr ibn Ali; and by al-Bayhaqi, al-Bayhaqi, and al-Baghawi via the path of Isma'il ibn Bishr ibn Mansur; all three ('Ayyash, Nasr ibn Ali, and Isma'il ibn Bishr) narrated it from Abd al-A'la through this chain. And Abd al-A'la was opposed in this hadith in two ways: opposed in its marfu' status and opposed in its mention of...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents an example of an acceptable increase (ziyada maqbula) in a hadith due to multiple narrators. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar describes raising hands at four points in prayer: opening takbir, bowing, rising from bowing, and standing up after two rak'ahs. The key point is that this narration includes the extra wording of raising hands at the fourth point (standing from two rak'ahs). This version is narrated by multiple reliable chains: from Abd al-A'la via three different transmitters ('Ayyash, Nasr ibn Ali, Isma'il ibn Bishr). Since the increase comes through multiple trustworthy narrators, it is accepted as part of the hadith. The passage then notes that Abd al-A'la was opposed in two ways: (1) some narrated it without the marfu' status (as a saying of Ibn Umar, not the Prophet), and (2) some narrations omitted the mention of the fourth raising. This illustrates the usul principle that when multiple reliable narrators agree on a ziyada, it is accepted over the version that lacks it.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer, a practice derived from prophetic example, especially at takbirat al-ihram, ruqu', and i'tidal.
زيادة (ziyada): An additional wording in a hadith not found in other narrations, here the mention of raising hands when standing after two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the increase (ziyada) in the hadith of raising hands considered acceptable according to the passage?
A) Because it was narrated by a single trustworthy narrator
B) Because it was narrated by multiple reliable narrators (the same narrator with multiple chains)
C) Because it agrees with the Shafi'i school
D) Because it is found in the Quran

Key Takeaway
A ziyada from a reliable narrator is accepted in Hanafi usul when it is supported by multiple chains, even if other chains omit it.

Accepting an Addition in Hadith: The Case of Raising Hands
Analysis of a hadith transmission and the acceptance of an addition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of accepting a trustworthy narrator's addition (ziyada) to a hadith and evaluate when the addition is accepted despite opposition.

Core Idea
A trustworthy narrator's addition is accepted if supported by multiple chains and not contradicted by stronger evidence.

The way hadiths are transmitted often involves variations. One narrator may add a detail that others omit. This lesson examines a case where the addition of raising hands when standing in prayer is accepted due to the abundance of narrators and the endorsement of Imam al-Bukhari. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrators and chains
List the narrators who support the addition and those who oppose it. Note that 'Abd al-A'la transmitted the version with the addition, while others transmitted it mawquf and without the addition.
The supporting narrators are 'Ayyash, Nasr ibn 'Ali, and Isma'il ibn Bishr, all via 'Abd al-A'la.
2
Note the type of opposition
The opposition is two-fold: some narrators transmitted the hadith as mawquf (stopped at Ibn 'Umar) instead of marfu' (attributed to the Prophet), and others omitted the specific mention of raising hands when standing from two rak'ahs.
The opposition includes Imam Malik and others.
3
Apply the principle of kathrat al-ruwat
The addition is supported by multiple chains through 'Abd al-A'la, even though many others transmitted without it. The abundance of narrators strengthens the addition.
Any principle from Hanafi usul: ziyadat al-thiqah maqbulah, especially when multiple chains support it.
4
Consider the authority of Bukhari
Imam al-Bukhari included the version with the addition in his Sahih, which is a strong endorsement of its authenticity.
Bukhari's inclusion is considered a validation of the addition.
5
Conclude the chosen position
The chosen position (al-mukhtar) is to accept the marfu' status and the addition, making the act of raising hands when standing from two rak'ahs part of the sunnah.
This conclusion is based on the weight of evidence and the principle of accepting a trustworthy narrator's addition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثال آخر للزيادة المقبولة بسبب كثرة الرواة روى عبد الأعلى عن عبيد الله بن عمر عن نافع أن عبد الله بن عمر كان إذا دخل في الصلاة كبر ورفع يديه، وإذا ركع رفع يديه، وإذا قال: سمع الله لمن حمده رفع يديه، وإذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه، رفع ذلك ابن عمر إلى النبي. هكذا رواه الإمام البخاري وابن حزم من طريق عياش، وأبو داود، والبيهقي من طريق نصر بن علي، والبيهقي، والبغوي من طريق إسماعيل بن بشر بن منصور؛ ثلاثتهم (عياش، ونصر بن علي، وإسماعيل بن بشر) رووه عن عبد الأعلى من هذا الوجه. وقد خولف عبد الأعلى في هذا الحديث مرتين: خولف في رفعه وخولف بذكر زيادة: «وإذا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه». فقد خالفه عبد الله بن إدريس وعبد الوهاب الثقفي والمعتمر بن سليمان فرووه عن عبيد الله عن نافع عن ابن عمر موقوفاً. وقد خولف عبد الأعلى لعدم ذكر الزيادة خالفه الإمام مالك فرواه عن نافع عن ابن عمر موقوفاً، بدون ذكر الزيادة. وخالفه أيضاً حماد بن سلمة وإبراهيم بن طهمان فروياه عن أيوب السختياني، ورواه ابن طهمان عن موسى بن عقبة. ورواه صالح بن كيسان؛ ثلاثتهم (أيوب، وموسى، وصالح)، عن نافع، عن ابن عمر موقوفاً. والمختار قبول الرفع وصحة الزيادة، فقد صححهما إمام المحدثين أبو عبد الله البخاري إذ أودعهما في صحيحه، وقد حكى الدارقطني في العلل الاختلاف في وقفة ورفعه وقال: «الأشبه بالصواب قول عبد الأعلى» نقله عنه الحافظ ابن حجر في فتح الباري ٢٢٢/٢.
Another example of an accepted addition due to the abundance of narrators: 'Abd al-A'la narrated from 'Ubayd Allah ibn 'Umar from Nafi' that 'Abd Allah ibn 'Umar used to, when entering prayer, say the takbir and raise his hands, and when bowing he raised his hands, and when he said 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' he raised his hands, and when he stood up from the two rak'ahs he raised his hands.' Ibn 'Umar attributed that to the Prophet. Thus narrated it Imam Bukhari and Ibn Hazm via 'Ayyash, and Abu Dawud and al-Bayhaqi via Nasr ibn 'Ali, and al-Bayhaqi and al-Baghawi via Isma'il ibn Bishr ibn Mansur; all three ('Ayyash, Nasr ibn 'Ali, and Isma'il ibn Bishr) narrated it from 'Abd al-A'la via this chain. And 'Abd al-A'la was opposed in this hadith twice: opposed in its marfu' status and opposed by the mention of the addition: 'and when he stood up from the two rak'ahs he raised his hands.' Indeed, 'Abd Allah ibn Idris, 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Thaqafi, and al-Mu'tamir ibn Sulayman opposed him and narrated it from 'Ubayd Allah from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar as mawquf. And 'Abd al-A'la was opposed regarding the omission of the addition: Imam Malik opposed him and narrated it from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar mawquf without mentioning the addition. Also, Hammad ibn Salama and Ibrahim ibn Tahman opposed him and narrated it from Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, and Ibn Tahman narrated it from Musa ibn 'Uqba. And Salih ibn Kisan narrated it; all three (Ayyub, Musa, and Salih) from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar mawquf. And the chosen position is to accept the marfu' status and the correctness of the addition, for Imam of the muhaddithin Abu 'Abd Allah al-Bukhari declared them authentic when he included them in his Sahih. Al-Daraqutni in al-'Ilal mentioned the disagreement in its stopping and raising and said: 'The closest to correctness is the statement of 'Abd al-A'la' as transmitted by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Fath al-Bari 2/222.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed example of how an addition (ziyada) in a hadith text, when narrated by a trustworthy narrator, is accepted over the versions of others who omit it. The hadith in question is about raising the hands in prayer. The narrator 'Abd al-A'la transmitted a version that includes raising the hands when standing from the two rak'ahs (tashahhud). Some other narrators transmitted the hadith as mawquf (stopped at Ibn 'Umar) and without that addition. The author notes that despite the opposition, the chosen position is to accept the marfu' version with the addition, because the number of narrators supporting it is abundant (kathrat al-ruwat) and because Imam al-Bukhari included it in his Sahih. This illustrates the usul principle that if a trustworthy narrator adds something that others do not, as long as it does not contradict a stronger source, the addition is accepted. The passage also highlights the importance of the abundance of narrators (kathrat al-ruwat) in strengthening a narration.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): An addition in the text of a hadith by a narrator that is not present in other versions.
رفع (raf'): Attribution of a statement or action to the Prophet (marfu'), as opposed to stopping at a companion (mawquf).
موقوف (mawquf): A hadith that is attributed to a companion and not to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the chosen position regarding the addition of raising hands when standing from two rak'ahs?
A) The addition is rejected because most narrators omit it.
B) The addition is accepted because it is reported by a trustworthy narrator and supported by Bukhari.
C) The addition is only accepted if narrated through tawatur.
D) The addition is accepted only as mawquf.

Key Takeaway
The chosen position is to accept the marfu' version with the addition due to the trustworthiness of the narrator and the abundance of chains.

Evaluating a Ziyada (Addition) in Hadith: The Case of Raising Hands
Examining chain variations and authenticity of the addition in Ibn Umar's hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding ziyada by identifying supporting chains (mutaba'at) and shawahid in contested narrations.

Core Idea
A reliable narrator's addition is accepted if supported by mutaba'at and shawahid, even if many others omitted it.

This lesson examines a controversial addition in the hadith of Ibn Umar about raising hands when standing from two rak'ahs. We will see how the Hanafi approach to evaluating ziyada works by analyzing the chains and concluding that the addition is sound, as authenticated by Imam al-Bukhari. Understanding this methodology is crucial for usul al-fiqh in weighing conflicting narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested addition and its narrator
Find the exact wording of the addition: 'وَإِذَا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه'. Note that it was narrated by 'Abd al-A'la from Nafi' from Ibn Umar as marfu'.
The addition refers to raising hands when standing after the first two rak'ahs.
2
Distinguish between marfu' and mawquf narrations
Separate the chains that narrate the hadith as mawquf (stopped at Ibn Umar) from those that narrate it as marfu' (raised to the Prophet). The opposition narrated it as mawquf without the addition.
A mawquf narration is considered weaker for establishing prophetic practice.
3
List the narrators who opposed 'Abd al-A'la
The author states that 'Abdullah bin Idris, 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Thaqafi, al-Mu'tamir, Imam Malik, Hammad bin Salama, and others narrated it mawquf without the addition.
These are the narrators who did not include the addition.
4
Analyze the supporting evidence: mutaba'at and shawahid
Identify the mutaba'at (follow-ups) that support 'Abd al-A'la's version, such as the narration from Muharib bin Dithar, and the shawahid (corroborating evidence) from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi.
Supporting chains strengthen the case for accepting the addition.
5
Apply the Hanafi usul principle on ziyada
Conclude that since the addition comes from a trustworthy narrator and is supported by mutaba'at and shawahid, and was authenticated by al-Bukhari, it is accepted. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that a ziyada from a reliable narrator is acceptable unless it contradicts a stronger source.
The acceptance of this addition has implications for fiqh rulings on raising hands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن زيادة: «وَإِذَا قام من الركعتين رفع يديه». فَقَدْ خالفه عَبْد الله بن إدريس وعبد الوهاب الثقفي، والمعتمر بن سليمان فرووه عن عبيد الله عن نافع عن ابن عُمر موقوفاً. وَقَدْ خولف عَبْد الأعلى لعدم ذكر الزيادة خالفه الإمام مالك) فرواه عن نافع، عن ابن عُمر موقوفاً، بدون ذكر الزيادة. وخالفه أيضاً حماد بن سلمة وإبراهيم بن طهمان فروياه عن أيوب السختياني، ورواه ابن طهمان عن موسى بن عُقْبَة. ورواه صالح بن كيسان؛ ثلاثتهم (أيوب، وموسى، وصالح)، عن نافع، عن ابن عمر؛ (والمختار قبول الرفع وصحة الزيادة، فَقَدْ صححهما إمام المُحَدِّثِينَ أبو عَبْد الله البُخَارِي إِذْ أودعهما في صحيحه، وَقَدْ حكى الدَّارَقُطني في العلل الاختلاف في وقفة ورفعه وَقَالَ: «الأشبه بالصواب قَوْل عَبْد الأعلى نقله عَنْهُ الحافظ ابن حجر في فتح الباري ٢٢٢/٢). إلا أن عبد الأعلى لم ينفرد بالحديث، فَقَدْ توبع عَلَيْهِ متابعات تامة ونازلة، تابعه عَلَى الرفع والزيادة محارب بن دثار فرواه عن عبد الله بن عُمَر. وتوبع عَلَى ذكر الزيادة أيضاً، لَكِنْ من طرق موقوفة عَلَى ابن عُمَر تابعه ابن جريج)، والليث بن سعد متابعة نازلة عن نافع إلا أنهم رووه موقوفاً وَقَدْ توبع عبد الأعلى بذكر الزيادة والرفع فرواه معتمر بن سليمان، عن عبيد الله بن عَبْد الله، عن الزُّهْرِيِّ، عن سالم، عن ابن عُمر بِهِ. وعبد الوهاب الثقفي)، عن عبيد الله عن الزُّهْرِيّ، عن نافع، عن ابن عمر، به. ثُمَّ إن لحديث عبد الأعلى بزيادته شواهد من حديث أبي حميد الساعدي، والإمام .(٢٨٨٤)
Chapter Three: Difference in chain and text. Addition: 'And when he stands from the two rak'ahs, he raises his hands.' So 'Abdullah bin Idris, 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Thaqafi, and al-Mu'tamir bin Sulayman opposed him and narrated it from 'Ubaydullah from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar as mawquf. And 'Abd al-A'la was opposed for not mentioning the addition: Imam Malik opposed him and narrated it from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar as mawquf without mentioning the addition. Also Hammad bin Salama and Ibrahim bin Tahman opposed him and narrated it from Ayyub al-Sakhtiyani, and Ibn Tahman narrated it from Musa bin 'Uqba. And Salih bin Kaysan narrated it; all three (Ayyub, Musa, and Salih) from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar. (The chosen position is to accept the raising and the authenticity of the addition, for the Imam of the hadith scholars Abu 'Abdullah al-Bukhari authenticated them when he placed them in his Sahih, and al-Daraqutni reported in al-'Ilal the difference regarding its stop and its raising and said: 'The closest to correctness is the statement of 'Abd al-A'la' as transmitted from him by al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar in Fath al-Bari 2/222). However, 'Abd al-A'la was not alone in the hadith, for he was followed in complete and low-level follow-ups. Muharib bin Dithar followed him in the raising and the addition and narrated it from 'Abdullah bin 'Umar. And he was followed in mentioning the addition also, but through chains that are mawquf upon Ibn 'Umar: Ibn Jurayj followed him, and al-Layth bin Sa'd in a low-level follow-up from Nafi', except they narrated it as mawquf. And 'Abd al-A'la was followed in mentioning the addition and the raising: al-Mu'tamir bin Sulayman narrated it from 'Ubaydullah bin 'Abdullah from al-Zuhri from Salim from Ibn 'Umar with it. And 'Abd al-Wahhab al-Thaqafi from 'Ubaydullah from al-Zuhri from Nafi' from Ibn 'Umar with it. Then, the hadith of 'Abd al-A'la with his addition has shawahid from the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, and the Imam. (2884)
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on differences in chain and text analyzes the hadith of Ibn Umar regarding raising hands when standing from the two rak'ahs. The author begins by noting the disagreement among narrators: some narrated the hadith with the addition 'and when he stands from the two rak'ahs, he raises his hands' as a marfu' (raised to the Prophet) narration, while others narrated it as mawquf (stopped at Ibn Umar) without the addition. The author lists the narrators who opposed 'Abd al-A'la (the one who reported the addition) and narrated it as mawquf. Then the author states the selected position: the addition is accepted and its authenticity is affirmed, citing that Imam al-Bukhari included it in his Sahih. The author then provides mutaba'at (follow-up chains) and shawahid (corroborating evidence) from other companions like Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi. This detailed analysis of chains and texts is fundamental in usul al-fiqh for determining the strength of a hadith which influences juristic rulings. Although the passage does not explicitly state a fiqh ruling, the acceptance of this addition would support the practice of raising hands during the prayer beyond the initial takbir, a point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The author's careful weighing of narrations demonstrates the methodology of hadith criticism used in deriving fiqh.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyāda): An additional phrase in a hadith text not found in other narrations of the same hadith.
رفع (raf'): Raising the hands during prayer; also used to describe a hadith attributed to the Prophet (marfu').
موقوف (mawqūf): A hadith narrated from a companion (not the Prophet) and attributed to that companion's statement or action.
متابعة (mutāba'a): A supporting chain that shares a common narrator with the main chain but at a higher level, strengthening the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the final assessment regarding the addition in the hadith of Ibn Umar?
A) It is rejected due to opposition from many narrators.
B) It is accepted and its authenticity is affirmed, as stated by the author.
C) It is considered uncertain and no preference is given.
D) It is only considered mawquf and not marfu'.

Key Takeaway
A ziyada from a reliable narrator, when supported by mutaba'at and shawahid, is accepted as authentic despite opposition from other trustworthy narrators.

Reconciling Conflicting Hadith: The Case of Raising Hands in Prayer
Critique of hadith authenticity and reconciliation of conflicting reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of takhsis (specification) to reconcile apparently contradictory hadith evidence, using the hadith of Ibn al-Zubayr and Ibn 'Umar on raising hands during prayer.

Core Idea
Weak chains can be strengthened by specific narrators, and apparent contradiction between hadith is resolved by specification (takhsis) rather than rejection.

In this lesson, we analyze a supporting hadith from Ibn al-Zubayr regarding raising hands during various postures of prayer, which seems to conflict with a sahih hadith from Ibn 'Umar. The commentator shows how the Hanafi method of reconciling texts through takhsis avoids claiming abrogation or weakness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the supporting hadith and its chain
The author presents a hadith from Abu Dawood via Qutayba from Ibn Lahi'a. Note the chain and the criticism of Ibn Lahi'a.
Qutayba's narration is considered good per Imam Ahmad.
2
Identify the opposing hadith
The hadith of Ibn 'Umar in Sahih al-Bukhari states that the Prophet did not raise hands except at takbirat al-ihram.
This is a sahih hadith.
3
Analyze the apparent contradiction
The two hadith seem to conflict: one indicates raising at multiple points, the other restricts.
The commentator in 'Awn al-Ma'bud claimed contradiction.
4
Apply the principle of takhsis
The author resolves by interpreting Ibn al-Zubayr's hadith as general ('amm) and Ibn 'Umar's as specific (khass), specifying its scope.
This avoids declaring either hadith weak or abrogated.
5
Derive the methodological lesson
The Hanafi usul prioritizes harmonization (jam') over contradiction or naskh when possible.
This is a key principle in dealing with conflicting texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن علي)، وأبي هُرَيْرَةَ). ٣٤٥ وهناك شاهد أخرجه أبو داود (۳)، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا قتيبة بن سعيد، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا ابن لهيعة، عن أبي هبيرة)، عن ميمون المكي)، أَنَّه رأى عَبْد الله بن الزبير وصلى بهم يشير بكفيه حِيْنَ يقوم، وحين يركع، وحين يسجد، وحين ينهض للقيام فيقوم فيشير بيديه، فانطلقت إلى ابن عَبَّاس فقلت: إني رأيت ابن الزُّبَيْر صلى صلاة لَمْ أر أحداً يصليها، فوصفت لَهُ هذِهِ الإشارة، فَقَالَ : إن أحببت أن تنظر إلى صلاة رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فاقتد بصلاة عَبْد الله بن الزُّبَيْر. وابن لهيعة وإن كَانَ فِيهِ مقال، إلا أن رِوَايَة قتيبة بن سعيد عَنْهُ جيدة، نَصَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الإمام المبجل أحمد بن حَنْبَل (٦) . وَقَدْ اعترض عَلَى هَذَا الحَدِيث صاحب عون المعبود فَقَالَ: «هَذَا يدل عَلَى مشروعية الرفع عِنْدَ القيام من السجود لَكِنَّهُ مَعَ ضعفه معارض بحديث ابن عُمـر المروي في صَحِيح البُخَارِيّ، وفيه: «ولا يفعل ذَلِكَ حِيْنَ يسجد وَلَا حِيْنَ يرفع رأسه من السجود). لكن الذي يبدو لي أن لا معارضة بَيْنَ الحديثين فيحمل حَدِيث ابن الزُّبَيْرِ عَلَى العموم، وحديث ابن عُمر مخصص له فخرج من العموم إلى الخصوص، وهذا أولى من ادعاء التعارض. و (١٨٧٦)، والبَيْهَقِي ٧٢/٢. (1) أخرجه أحمد (۹۳/۱ ، والبُخَارِيّ في جزء رفع اليدين» (۱) و (۹)، وأَبُو دَاوُد (٧٤٤) و(٧٦١)، وابن ماجه (٨٦٤) ، والتِّرْمِذِي (٣٤٢٣) ، وابن خزيمة (٥٨٤) ، والدَّارَقُطني ۲۸۷/۱، وذكر الخلال «علله» عن إسماعيل بن إسحاق الثقفي قَالَ: سئل أحمد عن حَدِيث عَلِي هَذَا فَقَالَ: صَحِيح. في انظر: نصب الراية ٤١٢/١). (٢) أخرجه أبو دَاوُد (۷۳۸)، وابن خزيمة (٦٩٤). (۳) في سننه (۷۳۹). (٤) هُوَ عَبْد الله بن هبيرة بن أسعد السبئي ،الحضرمي أبو هبيرة المصري: ثقة، توفي سنة (١٢٦ هـ). تهذيب الكمال ٣١٠/٤ (٣٦١٦) ، والكاشف (٦٠٥/١ (٣٠٣٣)، والتقريب (٣٦٧٨). I described this gesture to him, and he said: If you wish to see the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), then follow the prayer of 'Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr. And Ibn Lahi'a, although there is some criticism of him, the narration of Qutayba ibn Sa'id from him is good. The revered Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (6) explicitly stated that. And the author of 'Awn al-Ma'bud objected to this hadith, saying: 'This indicates the legitimacy of raising hands when rising from prostration, but despite its weakness, it is contradicted by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar reported in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'And he does not do that when prostrating nor when raising his head from prostration.' But it appears to me that there is no contradiction between the two hadiths. The hadith of Ibn al-Zubayr should be interpreted as general, and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is a specification of it, so it goes from general to specific, and this is preferable to claiming contradiction. Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a hadith regarding raising hands during prayer. The author begins by presenting a hadith from Abu Dawood via Qutayba ibn Sa'id from Ibn Lahi'a from Abu Hubayra from Maymun al-Makki, describing that he saw 'Abd Allah ibn al-Zubayr gesturing with his palms at various postures (standing, bowing, prostrating, rising). Ibn 'Abbas confirmed that this was the practice of the Prophet (pbuh). The author then addresses the criticism of the narration: although Ibn Lahi'a is considered weak, Qutayba's narration from him is deemed good by Imam Ahmad. Next, the author handles an objection by the commentator of 'Awn al-Ma'bud, who claimed this hadith contradicts another from Ibn 'Umar that denies such gestures during prostration and sujood. The author rejects the claim of contradiction, arguing that Ibn al-Zubayr's hadith is general ('amm) and Ibn 'Umar's hadith specifies (mukhassis) it, so they are harmonised without conflict. This shows the author's methodology of reconciling seemingly contradictory hadith by applying the principle of tahsis (specification). The passage concludes with footnotes providing additional references and identifying the narrators.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): The act of raising the hands during specific postures in prayer, specifically at takbirat al-ihram, ruku', sujood, and standing.
تخصيص (takhsis): The specification of a general ruling ('amm) by a more specific text (khass) to limit its application.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent contradiction between two texts that is resolved through reconciliation rather than claiming abrogation or weakness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author reconcile the apparent contradiction between the hadith of Ibn al-Zubayr (gesturing at sujood) and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (no gesture at sujood)?
A) He declares the hadith of Ibn al-Zubayr to be weak and inapplicable.
B) He claims the hadith of Ibn 'Umar is abrogated.
C) He interprets Ibn al-Zubayr's hadith as general and Ibn 'Umar's as a specification (takhsis).
D) He asserts they both refer to different types of gestures.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of takhsis (specification) allows reconciliation of seemingly contradictory hadith without rejecting any of them.

The Hanafi Position on Raising Hands: A Study in Dalil and Tarjih
Exposition of the two opinions on raising hands at bowing and rising from bowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi dalil for not raising hands except at the opening takbir, and apply the usul principle of tarjih when conflicting hadiths are presented.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school prioritizes the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura, teaching that stillness in prayer overrides other transmitted practices.

This passage from a work on the impact of hadith chains and texts on juristic differences presents a clear case study: the disagreement over raising the hands during prayer. We will examine how the Hanafi school uses the hadith of Jabir to support its position and how it responds to the opposing evidence from Ibn Umar's hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting hadiths
Locate the primary hadiths cited for each opinion: the hadith of Ibn Umar (supporting raising) and the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura (supporting stillness).
The passage lists many companions, but the core evidence is these two hadiths.
2
Assess transmission and textual clarity
Consider the thubut (certainty of transmission) and dalala (clarity of meaning) of each hadith. The Hanafis view the hadith of Jabir as having a clear command ('asikinu'), while the reports of raising are diffuse and may be subject to abrogation.
Both are ahad, but the Hanafis argue the explicit prohibition outweighs the narrated actions.
3
Apply Hanafi usul for contradictory evidence
The Hanafi school uses principles of tarjih: preference for a clear command (amr) over mere practice (fi'l), and consideration of abrogation (naskh) if the later hadith contradicts earlier practice.
The hadith of Jabir is taken as a later indication that the earlier practice was abrogated.
4
Determine the resulting ruling and thamarah
The Hanafi ruling: hands are raised only at the opening takbir. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis do not raise hands at bowing or rising, unlike Shafi'is.
This difference does not affect the validity of prayer; it is a difference in recommended practice.

Chapter Three: The Disagreement in Chain and Text. The Ruling of Raising the Hands in Prayer. There are multiple places where hands are raised in prayer; there occurred a great disagreement among scholars regarding its legitimacy. I will research this in issues: The First Issue: Raising the hands at bowing and at rising from it. The jurists disagreed on this in two opinions: The First Opinion: The hands are raised at bowing and at rising from it. Al-Shafi'i said: 'And indeed this has been narrated, besides Ibn Umar, by twelve men from the Prophet.' And al-Iraqi mentioned that it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from the hadith of fifty companions. The Second Opinion: The hands are not raised at bowing and at rising from it; rather they are raised only at the opening takbir. This is the opinion of Abu Bakr in a narration, Umar in a narration, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Umar in a narration, Ibn Abbas in a narration, al-Thawri, al-Sha'bi, al-Nakha'i, Ibn Abi Layla, al-Hasan ibn Salih ibn Hayy, al-Aswad, Alqama, Khaythama, Qays ibn Abi Hazim, Abu Ishaq al-Sabi'i. And Abu Hanifa and his companions went to this. And it is a narration from Malik, and it is the school of the people of Kufa. And they adduced the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out to us and said: Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be still in prayer.'
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the juristic disagreement on raising the hands during prayer, specifically at the time of bowing (rukū‘) and rising from bowing (raf‘ min al-rukū‘). The author first presents the first opinion, which holds that hands should be raised in both positions, and supports it by listing an extensive array of Companions, Successors, and later imams, including al-Shāfi‘ī, Aḥmad, and Ibn Ḥazm, as well as a narration from Mālik. Their primary evidence is the well-known hadith of Ibn ‘Umar, which reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to raise his hands at the opening takbīr, at bowing, and at rising from bowing. Al-Shāfi‘ī is quoted emphasizing that this hadith is transmitted by twelve other companions besides Ibn ‘Umar, while al-‘Irāqī mentions it is narrated from fifty companions. The second opinion, which is the Ḥanafī position, holds that hands are raised only at the opening takbīr, not at bowing or rising. This is attributed to several Companions and Successors, and is the position of Abū Ḥanīfa and his followers, as well as a narration from Mālik and the school of Kūfa. Their evidence is the hadith of Jābir ibn Samura, in which the Prophet reproached some companions for raising their hands during prayer, comparing them to the tails of restive horses, and commanded stillness. The Ḥanafīs interpret this hadith as indicating that raising hands beyond the opening takbīr is not part of the established practice. The author here is demonstrating how differences in hadith transmission (asānīd) and textual interpretation (mutūn) lead to differences in juristic rulings, which is the core theme of the book.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf‘ al-yadayn): The act of raising both hands to the level of the shoulders or ears during prayer
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbīrat al-iḥrām): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' that commences the prayer
أسكنوا (asikinū): Be still, be calm (imperative command in the hadith of Jabir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, at which point(s) in the prayer should the hands be raised?
A) At the opening takbir only
B) At the opening takbir, at bowing, and at rising from bowing
C) At bowing only
D) At no point

Key Takeaway
The dispute over raising hands illustrates that different hadiths and their interpretations, not disregard for sunnah, lead to juristic differences within the framework of shared principles.

Raising Hands in Prayer: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i Evidence
Presentation of two opinions with their hadith evidence and criticisms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on raising hands in prayer by analyzing their respective hadith evidence and identifying the usul principles underlying the disagreement.

Core Idea
Hanafis restrict raising hands to opening takbir; Shafi'is extend it to ruku' and rising — the dispute hinges on interpretation and authentication of hadith.

This lesson delves into the classic dispute over raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer. You will examine the hadith evidence presented by both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, analyze the criticisms of each proof, and understand how differences in textual interpretation lead to divergent fiqh rulings. By the end, you will be able to articulate the Hanafi position and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions and their proponents
List the schools and narrations that hold each view. Note that the Hanafi position restricts raising hands to the opening takbir, while the Shafi'i position extends it to ruku' and rising.
Pay attention to the list of Companions and early scholars supporting each side.
2
Extract the primary evidence for each side
For the Shafi'i view: the hadith of Ibn Umar. For the Hanafi view: the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura and the practice of Ibn Mas'ud. Write down the key phrases.
Consider the wording of Jabir's hadith: 'Be calm in prayer' and the metaphor of horses' tails.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafis argue that Jabir's hadith is general and prohibits raising hands except at the opening takbir. They also critique the Shafi'i interpretation by citing Bukhari's comment that Jabir's hadith refers specifically to tashahhud.
Bukhari's comment shows a textual interpretation difference.
4
Evaluate the criticisms of the Hanafi evidence
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is criticized by hadith critics like Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, Abu Hatim, and Abu Dawud. Assess whether this weakens the Hanafi position or if their primary evidence (Jabir's hadith) stands independently.
Consider the role of hadith criticism in fiqh disputes.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
This disagreement results in a different practice: Hanafis do not raise hands at ruku' and rising, while Shafi'is do. Understand how this affects the worshipper.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in prayer.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن وأحمد (۱) وابن حزم (۳) وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن مَالِك (۳) واستدلوا بحديث ابن عُمر المتقدم). قَالَ الشَّافِعِيّ: (وَقَدْ رَوَى هَذَا سوى ابن عُمَر اثنا عشر رجلاً عن النبي (). وذكر العراقي أنه مروي عن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من حديث خمسين صحابيا). القول الثاني: لا ترفع اليدان عِنْدَ الركوع وعِنْدَ الرفع مِنْهُ، وإنما ترفعان عِنْدَ تكبيرة الإحرام فقط. وَهُوَ قَوْل أَبي بَكْر في رِوَايَة، وعمر في رِوَايَة، وعلي وابن مَسْعُود، وابن عُمَر في رِوَايَة، وابن عَبَّاس في رِوَايَة والثَّوْرِيّ، والشعبي، والنخعي، وابن أبي ليلى، والحَسَن بن صالح بن حيّ، والأسود، وعلقمة، وخيثمة، وقيس بن أبي حازم، وأبي إسحاق السَّبِيعِيّ ، وإِليه ذهب أبو حَنِيْفَة وأصحابه (۸)، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن مَالِك (٤) وَهُوَ مَذْهَب أهل الكوفة (١). واستدلوا بحديث جابر بن سمر ة (١١) قَالَ: «خَرَجَ عَلَيْنَا رَسُوْلَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: مالي أراكم رافعي أيديكم كأنها أذناب خيل شمس أسكنوا في الصَّلاة (١٢). وبما روي عن ابن مَسْعُود أَنَّهُ قَالَ: ألا أصلي بكم صلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى وَلَمْ يرفع يديه إلا في أول مرة). وَقَالَ البُخَارِيّ مُعلقاً عَلَى حَدِيث جابر بن سمرة: «فإنما كَانَ هَذَا في التشهد لا في القيام كَانَ يُسلم بعضهم عَلَى بَعْض فنهى النَّبي لا عن رفع الأيدي في التشهد، وَلاَ يحتج بهذا من له حظ من العِلْم هَذَا مَعْرُوف مَشْهُور لا اختلاف فِيهِ، وَلَوْ كَانَ كَمَا ذهب إليه لكان رفع الأيدي في أول التكبيرة وأيضاً تكبيرات العيد منهياً عَنْهَا؛ لأَنَّهُ لَمْ يستثن رفعاً دُونَ رفع وَقَدْ ثبت حَدِيث»(۲). أما حَدِيث ابن مسعود فضعفه عبد الله بن المبارك فَقَالَ: «لَمْ يثبت»(۳). وقال أبو حاتم الرازي: «هَذَا خطأ» (٤) . وَقَالَ أَبو داود: «لَيْسَ هُوَ بصحيح عَلَى هَذَا اللفظ». إلا أن الزيدية أنكروا رفع اليدين عند الإحرام).
Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. And Ahmad (1) and Ibn Hazm (3) and it is a narration from Malik (3) and they argued with the hadith of Ibn Umar previously mentioned. Al-Shafi'i said: 'This has been narrated, besides Ibn Umar, by twelve men from the Prophet.' And al-Iraqi mentioned that it is narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from the hadith of fifty Companions. The second opinion: Hands are not raised at the time of bowing and at the time of rising from it, rather they are raised only at the takbir of ihram. This is the saying of Abu Bakr in one narration, and Umar in one narration, and Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar in one narration, and Ibn Abbas in one narration, and al-Thawri, al-Sha'bi, al-Nakha'i, Ibn Abi Layla, al-Hasan ibn Salih ibn Hayy, al-Aswad, 'Alqama, Khaythama, Qays ibn Abi Hazim, and Abu Ishaq al-Sabi'i, and this is what Abu Hanifa and his companions went to (8), and it is a narration from Malik (4), and it is the school of the people of Kufa (1). They argued with the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura (11) who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out to us and said: "What is wrong with me that I see you raising your hands as if they are tails of restive horses? Be calm in prayer" (12). And with what was narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he said: 'Shall I not pray with you the prayer of the Prophet (peace be upon him)? So he prayed and did not raise his hands except the first time.' Al-Bukhari commented on the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura: 'This was only during the tashahhud, not during standing; they used to greet each other, so the Prophet forbade raising hands during tashahhud. One with a share of knowledge cannot use this as evidence. This is well-known, famous, no difference about it. If it were as they claim, then raising hands at the first takbir and also the takbirs of 'Eid would be forbidden, because he did not exempt one raising over another, and the hadith is established.' As for the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak weakened it, saying: 'It is not established.' Abu Hatim al-Razi said: 'This is a mistake.' Abu Dawud said: 'It is not authentic in this wording.' However, the Zaydis denied raising hands at the takbir of ihram.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the issue of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the prayer positions. The first opinion, attributed to Shafi'i, Ahmad, Ibn Hazm, and a narration from Malik, holds that hands are raised at the bowing (ruku') and when rising from it, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar. The second opinion, which is the Hanafi position, restricts raising hands to the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) only. This is also the view of many Companions and the Kufan school. The Hanafis cite the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura, where the Prophet forbade raising hands like horses' tails, which they interpret as a general prohibition except for the opening takbir. They also rely on the practice of Ibn Mas'ud, who demonstrated the prayer without raising except at the start. The Shafi'i counterargument from al-Bukhari interprets Jabir's hadith as specific to tashahhud, not general prayer, and argues that if it were general, it would also prohibit raising at the opening takbir and 'Eid takbirs, which are established. Furthermore, the Hanafis' second proof (Ibn Mas'ud's hadith) is criticized by hadith critics as weak or erroneous. The Zaydis even denied raising at the opening takbir altogether. This lesson shows how differences in hadith interpretation and authenticity lead to divergent fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): The act of lifting both hands during specific prayer positions, often up to the ears or shoulders.
تكبيرة الإحرام (takbirat al-ihram): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' that commences the prayer.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Hadith of Jabir ibn Samura
C) Hadith of Abu Hurairah
D) Hadith of Aisha

Key Takeaway
The dispute on raising hands in prayer demonstrates how differences in hadith interpretation and authenticity assessment lead to divergent fiqh rulings, emphasizing the role of usul al-fiqh in resolving such conflicts.

Evaluating a Transmitter's Addition: Raising Hands in Prayer
Presenting two opinions on raising hands when rising to the third rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the evidentiary weight of a transmitter's addition (ziyada) in a hadith and apply Hanafi usul principles to derive a fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
A transmitter's addition may be accepted or rejected based on reliability and consistency with the more authentic practice.

Differences in hadith transmission often lead to differences in fiqh rulings. In this passage, the addition of a transmitter named 'Abd al-A'la is used to argue for raising hands when standing from the first tashahhud. Understanding how Hanafi usul evaluates such additions helps us see why the Hanafi school maintains its position of not raising hands except at the opening takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Act
Determine the specific act in dispute: raising the hands when rising from the first tashahhud to the third rak'ah.
This is separate from the general debate on raf' al-yadayn in other positions.
2
State the Two Opinions
First opinion: hands are raised (supported by several Companions and later scholars). Opposing opinion: hands are not raised (the position of the Hanafi school and others).
3
Examine the Evidence for the First Opinion
The first opinion relies on a 'ziyada' (addition) in a hadith transmitted by 'Abd al-A'la. Identify that this addition is the key proof.
The exact text of the addition is not quoted in the passage but is referenced as 'زيادة عبد الأعلى السابقة الذكر'.
4
Apply Hanafi Usul: The Rule on Ziyada
Recall the Hanafi principle: a trustworthy transmitter's addition is accepted if it does not contradict the more widely transmitted version or the established practice (amal). Evaluate the addition here against the majority practice.
The Hanafi school prioritizes 'umum al-balwa' and the more authentic hadiths that restrict raf' to the opening takbir.
5
Derive the Hanafi Ruling
Conclude that the addition is considered shadhdh (irregular) and is not a valid basis for sunniyyah; thus the Hanafi ruling is not to raise hands.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية: هَلْ ترفع اليدان في مَوْضِع آخر ، وَهُوَ عِنْدَ القيام من التشهد الأول إلى الركعة الثالثة عَلَى قولين: القَوْل الأول : ترفع اليدان عند القيام من الركعتين. وهذا القَوْل رَواهُ الإِمَام عَلِيّ، وأبو حميد الساعدي في عَشْرَة من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيهم أبو قتادة (1) . وَهُوَ قَوْل ابن عُمَر (3) وعطاء)، والبخاري(4). وإليه ذهب بغض أصحاب الشَّافِعِيّ () ، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الإمام أحمد ()، وابن حزم (V) . مستدلين بزيادة عبد الأعلى السابقة الذكر والتفصيل وخالف في ذَلِكَ جَمَاعَة من أهل العِلْم (۸) فلم يروا رفع اليدين في هَذَا الموضع.

This passage presents the second issue of raf' al-yadayn: whether to raise hands when standing from the first tashahhud to the third rak'ah. The first opinion, supported by several Companions and later scholars, holds that hands should be raised. Their evidence is the 'addition' (ziyada) of 'Abd al-A'la (likely a transmitter who added this detail in a hadith) and the general practice. The opposing group, which includes many scholars (including Hanafis by implication), does not raise hands here. The author cites the supporters but does not detail the second opinion's evidence.

Key Terms
التشهد الأول (al-tashahhud al-awwal): The first sitting for tashahhud after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or four rak'ahs.
زيادة (ziyada): An addition in a hadith transmitted by one narrator that is not found in other chains.

Evaluating Weak Evidences: Raising Hands During Sujud
First opinion with critical evaluation of its evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a Hanafi usuli considers a hadith-based position weak and apply the principle that unauthenticated traditions cannot support a ruling.

Core Idea
Weak traditions (la tathbut) cannot establish a fiqh ruling in the Hanafi school.

This passage presents one side of a celebrated dispute: whether to raise the hands when going into prostration and rising from it. The author lists many early scholars who supported the practice, but immediately undercuts their position by noting that the traditions they rely on are not authentic. As a student of usul, you must learn to separate authority of names from authority of evidence. This lesson walks you through how a Hanafi usuli evaluates the thubut (reliability) of a reported hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the first opinion
State the fiqh issue and the first opinion exactly as given. Note which scholars held it (companions, tabi'un, later figures).
The author gives a long list—do not confuse quantity of names with strength of evidence.
2
Locate the author's critical remark
Find the phrase where the author comments on the dalil. The text says: 'وَقَدْ جاءت بِذَلِكَ آثار لا تثبت' — 'traditions have come about that are not established.'
The word 'لا تثبت' indicates the traditions are weak in chain (thubut) or content.
3
Classify the evidence type
The author mentions that the supporters used a hadith ('واستدلوا بحديث'). Since only a fragment is given, we know it is a hadith ahad (not mutawatir). In Hanafi usul, ahad hadith give zanni knowledge.
Identify thubut as zanni and dalala as not yet assessed.
4
Apply the Hanafi principĺe of evidence acceptance
For a hadith to be used as dalil, it must be authentic (sahih) in thubut. The author explicitly says the traditions are not established, so they cannot override the established practice or other stronger proofs.
Hanafi usul requires that a hadith be mashhur or sahih to be used for wajib rulings; weak (da'if) hadith are not sufficient.
5
Determine the resulting methodological lesson
The passage teaches that listing many scholars does not make a position strong; it is the reliability of the transmitted evidence that matters. This is a core lesson in talil (reasoning) and naqd (critique).
The second opinion (not raising hands) is not given, but the implication is that it is stronger because its evidence is authentic.

Commentary
This passage begins the third issue: whether to raise hands when going into sujud and when rising from it. The first opinion, attributed to many early scholars and hadith experts, supports raising at these points. However, the author immediately notes that the traditions (athar) supporting this are not authentic (la tathbut). The text cuts off at 'they used as evidence the hadith...', so the proof is not given here. The opposing opinion (not raising) is not yet presented, but the implication is that the majority of Hanafi scholars do not raise hands in these positions.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration, a pillar of prayer where the forehead, nose, palms, knees, and toes touch the ground.
آثار (athar): Traditions, reports from the Prophet (ﷺ) or his companions; sometimes used synonymously with hadith.
لا تثبت (la tathbut): It is not established; i.e., the report is not authentic in its chain or content.

Key Takeaway

Raising Hands Between Prostrations: Waa'il vs. Ibn Umar
Analyzing a dispute over raising hands between prostrations due to conflicting hadiths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tarjih when two hadiths conflict, using the example of raising hands between prostrations.

Core Idea
When hadiths conflict, preference is given to the narration of the companion with longer companionship.

This lesson examines a classical example of hadith conflict resolution: the raising of hands between prostrations. The Hanafi school relies on the principle that an addition (ziyada) from a trustworthy narrator is generally accepted, but when it contradicts a more reliable narration, the latter takes precedence. Ibn Abd al-Barr's analysis in al-Tamhid illustrates this tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
State what each narrator reports: Waa'il ibn Hujr reports raising hands between prostrations; Ibn Umar reports the Prophet did not raise them.
Note that both are sahabi narrations.
2
Assess the reliability of each narrator
Consider the duration of companionship: Waa'il only saw the Prophet for a few days; Ibn Umar accompanied him until his death. This makes Ibn Umar's report more reliable.
3
Apply the principle of tarjih
When two hadiths conflict and cannot be reconciled, the more reliable narration is preferred. Here, Ibn Umar's is preferred due to longer companionship.
Hanafi usul accepts additions from trustworthy narrators, but not when they contradict a stronger report.
4
Derive the ruling
The ruling is that hands are not raised between prostrations or when rising from them. This is the position of the majority (jumhur).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ ابن عبد البر في التمهيد زيادة وائل بن حجر في حديثه رفع اليدين بَيْنَ السجدتين قَدْ عارضه في ذَلِكَ ابن عُمَر بقوله: «وَكَانَ لا يرفع بَيْنَ السجدتين»، والسنن لا تثبت إذا تعارضت وتدافعت ووائل بن حجر إنما رآه أياماً قليلة في قدومه عَلَيْهِ، وابن عُمَر صحبه إِلَى أن تُوُفِّي الله فحديث ابن عُمَر أصح عندهم وأولى أن يُعمل بِهِ». القول الثاني: لا ترفع اليدان عند السجود وعند الرفع مِنْهُ وَهُوَ مَذْهَب الْجُمْهُور).
And Ibn Abd al-Barr said in al-Tamhid: The addition of Waa'il ibn Hujr in his hadith of raising the hands between the two prostrations is opposed by Ibn Umar with his statement: 'And he would not raise between the two prostrations.' And sunan are not established when they conflict and contradict. Waa'il ibn Hujr only saw him (the Prophet) for a few days during his arrival to him, while Ibn Umar accompanied him until Allah took him. So the hadith of Ibn Umar is more authentic according to them and more deserving to be acted upon. The second opinion: Hands are not raised during prostration and when rising from it, and this is the majority's madhhab.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding raising hands between prostrations. The author quotes Ibn Abd al-Barr's tarjeeh from al-Tamhid. The core issue is a conflict between two hadiths: Waa'il ibn Hujr reports raising hands between prostrations, while Ibn Umar reports that the Prophet did not do so. Ibn Abd al-Barr gives preference to Ibn Umar because of his longer companionship with the Prophet, making his narration more reliable. He also notes that sunan (established practices) are not considered established if they conflict and contradict. The second opinion states that hands are not raised at all during prostration and rising from it, which is the position of the majority (jumhur).

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): An addition in a hadith not found in other versions
تدافع (tadāfu'): Mutual contradiction between hadiths such that both cannot be sound

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When hadiths conflict, the more reliable narration due to longer companionship is given precedence.

Five Opinions on Hand-Raising Height in Prayer Takbir
Listing five scholarly opinions on how high to raise hands during takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five scholarly opinions on raising hands during the opening takbir, state the Hanafi position with its evidence, and explain why multiple positions are valid.

Core Idea
Differences in hadith transmission produce multiple valid rulings on hand-raising height.

This passage demonstrates a classic example of ikhtilaf arising from different authentic hadith transmissions. Five distinct opinions are recorded, each attributed to companions and imams. The Hanafi school follows raising hands to the ears, while the Shafi'i school follows raising to the shoulders. Understanding the basis of these differences is essential for appreciating valid diversity within Sunni fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five opinions
List each of the five opinions mentioned: 1) to shoulders, 2) to ears, 3) to chest, 4) choice between shoulders and ears, 5) above the head.
Note the fifth opinion is rejected as baseless.
2
Note the proponents and evidence for the first two opinions
For opinion 1 (shoulders): proponents include Umar, Ibn Umar, etc., and evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar. For opinion 2 (ears): proponents include Abu Hanifa, and evidence is the hadith of Waa'il ibn Hujr.
Both hadith are considered authentic; the difference is a matter of preference.
3
Recognize the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi school adheres to raising hands to the ears. This is based on the hadith of Waa'il ibn Hujr, which is preferred in Hanafi usul due to its narrators.
Other schools, like Shafi'i, prefer the hadith of Ibn Umar.
4
Understand the treatment of the fifth opinion
The fifth opinion (above the head) is explicitly rejected as having no basis. This shows that not all transmitted opinions are accepted; weak or fabricated narrations are discarded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الرابعة: إلى أين ترفع اليدان، وَفِي ذَلِكَ أقوال:
القَوْل الأول: ترفع اليدان إلى حذو المنكبين. وَهُوَ قَوْل عُمَر، وأبي هُرَيْرَة، وابن عُمَر وعبد الله بن الزُّبَيْر، وأم الدرداء، وسالم، ونافع، ومحمد بن سيرين وطاووس، وعطاء، والقاسم، ومكحول، وإسحاق). وَهُوَ المشهور عن مالك()، وإليه ذهب الشَّافِعِيّ ) ، وَهُوَ المشهور عن أحمد ) . واستدلوا بحديث ابن عمر ).
القَوْل الثاني: ترفع اليدان إلى حذو الأذنين. وَهُوَ قَوْل عطاء، ووهب بن منبه، وأبي جَعْفَر، وإبراهيم، والثَّوْرِيّ. وإليه ذهب أبو حَنِيْفَة ) ، وروي ذَلِكَ عن أحمد ()، وَهُوَ قَوْل ابن حبيب من المالكية (۳). واستدلوا بحديث وائل.
القَوْلِ الثَّالث: ترفع اليدان إلى الصدر. وَهُوَ قَوْل للإمام مالك (٥) ورواية عن الإمام أحمد ().
القَوْل الرابع: التخيير بَيْنَ رفع اليدين إلى الأذنين أو المنكبين. وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الإمام أحمد ()، وحكاه ابن المنذر عن بَعْض أهل الحديث واستحسنه (۸).
القَوْل الخامس: ترفع اليدان حَتَّى تجاوزا الرأس في تكبيرة الافتتاح. هَذَا القَوْل حكاه العبيدي عن طاووس، وَهُوَ قَوْل ابنه، وهذا باطل لا أصل لَهُ ).
The fourth issue: To where are the hands raised? And there are opinions about that: The first opinion: The hands are raised to the level of the shoulders. This is the statement of Umar, Abu Hurairah, Ibn Umar, Abdullah ibn al-Zubair, Umm al-Darda', Salim, Nafi', Muhammad ibn Sirin, Tawus, Ata', al-Qasim, Makhul, and Ishaq. And it is the well-known from Malik, and al-Shafi'i went to it, and it is the well-known from Ahmad. And they adduced the hadith of Ibn Umar. The second opinion: The hands are raised to the level of the ears. This is the statement of Ata', Wahb ibn Munabbih, Abu Ja'far, Ibrahim, and al-Thawri. And Abu Hanifa went to it, and it is narrated from Ahmad, and it is the statement of Ibn Habib of the Malikis. And they adduced the hadith of Waa'il. The third opinion: The hands are raised to the chest. This is a statement of Imam Malik and a narration from Imam Ahmad. The fourth opinion: Choice between raising the hands to the ears or the shoulders. This is a narration from Imam Ahmad, and Ibn al-Mundhir narrated it from some hadith experts and deemed it good. The fifth opinion: The hands are raised until they go past the head in the opening takbir. This opinion was narrated by al-Ubaidi from Tawus, and it is the statement of his son, and this is false with no basis.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage enumerates five different scholarly opinions regarding the height to which one should raise the hands during the opening takbir of prayer. Each opinion is attributed to specific Companions, Successors, or imams. The Hanafi position is the second opinion: raising hands to the ears. This is based on the hadith of Waa'il ibn Hujr. The first opinion (to shoulders) is supported by the hadith of Ibn Umar and is the view of al-Shafi'i and the well-known view of Ahmad. The third (to chest) is a minority view. The fourth allows a choice. The fifth (above the head) is rejected as baseless.

Key Terms
حذو المنكبين (ḥadhw al-mankibayn): Level with the shoulders
حذو الأذنين (ḥadhw al-udhnayn): Level with the ears

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) To the ears
C) To the chest
D) Above the head

Key Takeaway
Multiple authentic transmissions yield multiple valid rulings; the Hanafi school raises hands to the ears based on the hadith of Waa'il.

Al-Shafi'i's Jam' Conflicting Hadiths on Hand Position
Explaining how al-Shafi'i harmonizes conflicting hadiths on hand height

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of jam' (reconciliation) to conflicting hadiths and explain how al-Shafi'i harmonized the reports on hand position during takbir.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i reconciled conflicting hadiths by applying all of them: palms at shoulders, thumbs at earlobes, fingertips at ear tops.

In this brief passage, we see al-Shafi'i's practical application of the usul principle of jam' (reconciliation). When faced with apparently contradictory hadiths about raising hands to shoulders versus ears, he did not choose one over the other; instead, he combined the reports into a single posture, satisfying all narrations. This demonstrates a key method of dealing with ikhtilaf, prioritizing reconciliation over preference when possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting reports
Recognize that one set of hadiths indicates raising hands to the shoulders, while another indicates raising to the ears.
These are both authentic reports from different companions.
2
State al-Shafi'i's reconciliation
He placed his palms level with his shoulders and his thumbs/fingertips at his earlobes/ear tops, thus incorporating both descriptions in a single action.
3
Understand the usul principle
This is an example of jam' (reconciliation), which applies all conflicting texts rather than rejecting or preferring one over the other.
Jam' is preferred over tarjeeh (preference) when a plausible combination exists.
4
Recognize the scope
This method is used when the texts can be physically or practically combined without contradiction.
If combination is impossible, other methods like tarjeeh or naskh are considered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة:
الشَّافِعِي بَيْنَ هَذِهِ الأحاديث فيقول: يجعل كفيه حذو منكبيه، وإبهاميه ويجمع عِنْدَ شحمة أذنيه، ورؤوس أصابعه عِنْدَ فروع أذنيه (١٠).
Benefit: Al-Shafi'i reconciled these hadiths by saying: He places his palms level with his shoulders, and his thumbs and brings them together at his earlobes, and the tips of his fingers at the tops of his ears.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This is a brief benefit (faaidah) showing how al-Shafi'i reconciled the different reports about hand placement. Instead of choosing one position exclusively, he combined them: the palms are aligned with the shoulders, while the thumbs are near the earlobes and fingertips at the top of the ears. This way, both the shoulder-level and ear-level narrations are satisfied in a single action.

Key Terms
جمع (jam'): Reconciliation of seemingly conflicting hadiths by applying all of them

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Palms at shoulders.
B) Thumbs at ears.
C) Palms at shoulders and thumbs at ears.
D) Palms at ears and thumbs at shoulders.

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i reconciled conflicting hand-position hadiths by performing both simultaneously, demonstrating the usul principle of jam'.

Identifying Erroneous Additions in Hadith: The Principle of al-Ziyādah Khaṭa’
Introducing an example where an addition in a hadith is identified as an error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi methodology to identify when an addition in a hadith is deemed an error and explain the rationale for rejecting such additions.

Core Idea
Not every addition in a hadith is reliable—some are identified as errors through careful textual and chain analysis.

In hadith criticism, not all narrations are equally reliable. An addition (ziyādah) may seem to provide extra detail, but scholars have long recognized that some additions are mistakes. This lesson introduces the principle of 'al-ziyādah khaṭa’' (the addition is an error) and walks through how Hanafi usulis evaluate such cases, using an incomplete but instructive example from the source text.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Principle
Learn that al-ziyādah khaṭa’ is a methodological tool: an addition in a hadith that conflicts with stronger, more reliable narrations is deemed erroneous and rejected.
This principle is applied after comparing multiple chains and texts.
2
Recognize the Context
The source passage sets up an example: a narration from Abd al-Razzaq via Ma'mar from Thabit and Qatada from Anas. The text cuts off, but the title indicates that this example was investigated and the addition found to be an error.
Even incomplete, it shows that the scholar (likely the author of the original work) demonstrated that not all additions are accepted.
3
Analyze the Chain and Text
Consider the narrators and the content. The addition 'Here is water' after a companion looked for water and did not find it may be problematic because it contradicts the context of finding no water—possibly a case of mixing narrations.
Hanafi usulis examine both sanad and matn; inconsistencies often point to error.
4
Apply the Methodology
When encountering a hadith with an addition, compare with all parallel narrations. If the addition appears only in a weak chain or disrupts the logical flow, it is likely a mistake.
The principle of 'al-ziyādah khaṭa’' is not absolute—it depends on the overall reliability of the transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثال ما حقق فيه أن الزيادة خطأ :
ما أخرجه عَبْد الرزاق (۱۱) ، قَالَ : أخبرنا معمر عن ثابت وقتادة، عن أنس، قَالَ: «نظر بَعْض أصحاب النَّبي وضوءاً فلم يجده ، فَقَالَ النَّبيِّ : ها هنا ماء فرأيت
An example of what was investigated where the addition is an error: What Abd al-Razzaq narrated, he said: Ma'mar informed us from Thabit and Qatada, from Anas, who said: 'Some of the companions of the Prophet looked for water but did not find it, so the Prophet said: Here is water, then I saw...'
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage introduces an example showing that an addition in a hadith can be determined to be an error. It begins quoting a narration from Abd al-Razzaq via Ma'mar from Thabit and Qatada from Anas, but the text ends abruptly. The full example likely demonstrates which addition is wrong and why, but we cannot see the conclusion. This illustrates that not every ziyadah (addition) is automatically accepted; it must be checked for correctness.

Key Terms
الزيادة خطأ (al-ziyādah khaṭa’): An addition in a hadith that is determined to be a mistake after investigation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That additions in hadith are always accepted
B) That some additions in hadith are errors
C) The correct method of ablution
D) The reliability of Abd al-Razzaq

Key Takeaway
Additions in hadith must be scrutinized; if they conflict with stronger narrations, they may be deemed errors and rejected.

Identifying an Erroneous Addition: The Case of Ma'mar's 'Bismillah'
Analyzes a hadith to prove an addition is erroneous

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an erroneous addition (ziyādah khaṭaʾ) in a hadith by comparing narrations and applying the Hanafi principle that tafarrud (solitary narration) against a majority indicates error.

Core Idea
An addition in a hadith is erroneous if a single narrator is contradicted by the majority of reliable narrators.

This lesson presents a concrete case from Hanafi usul al-hadith. We examine a hadith about the Prophet's miracle of water flowing from his fingers. The narrator Ma'mar ibn Rashid added the phrase 'Bismillah'. By comparing his narration with the many other reliable narrations that omit it, the author demonstrates how to identify an erroneous addition. This method is essential for evaluating the strength of ahadith before using them for legal derivation (istinbat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested phrase
Locate the addition of 'Bismillah' in Ma'mar's version of the hadith. This is the phrase whose authenticity is in question.
The hadith describes the Prophet making water flow from his fingers.
2
List the narrators of the addition
Note that Ma'mar ibn Rashid is the only narrator who includes 'Bismillah' in this chain. He is trustworthy, but alone in this addition.
Ma'mar is a thiqah, but tafarrud is significant.
3
List the narrators who omit it
Identify the many other narrators from the same sources (Thabit and Qatada) who do not mention 'Bismillah'. The passage lists multiple chains via Sulayman ibn al-Mughira and others.
The majority of narrators from Thabit and Qatada omit the phrase.
4
Apply the principle of tafarrud
Recognize that Ma'mar is tafarrada bihi (alone in adding). In Hanafi usul, if a single narrator adds something not found in the narrations of equally or more reliable narrators, the addition is considered weak (shadhdh or munkar).
Trustworthiness does not protect against memory error.
5
Conclude on the addition
Based on the comparison, the addition is deemed erroneous (ziyādah khaṭaʾ) and is rejected. It is not part of the authentic hadith.
This conclusion impacts any fiqh ruling that might rely on this phrase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Benefit: Al-Shafi'i between these ahadith says: He places his palms opposite his shoulders, and his thumbs and collects at his earlobes, and the tips of his fingers at the ends of his ears (10). An example of what has been verified as an erroneous addition: What 'Abd al-Razzaq narrated (11), he said: Ma'mar informed us from Thabit and Qatada, from Anas, who said: 'One of the companions of the Prophet looked for water for ablution but did not find it. The Prophet said: Here is water. I saw the Prophet put his hand in the vessel containing water, then said: Perform ablution, by Allah. I saw the water flowing from between his fingers, and the people performed ablution until they all had done so.' And Ma'mar, the shaykh of 'Abd al-Razzaq, is Ma'mar ibn Rashid al-Azdi, trustworthy, reliable, virtuous (2), and his two shaykhs in this hadith are Thabit ibn Aslam al-Bunani, who is trustworthy and devout (3), and Qatada ibn Di'ama al-Sadusi, who is trustworthy and reliable. However, Ma'mar ibn Rashid erred by mentioning the addition 'Bismillah' in the hadith, since the majority of narrators from Thabit and Qatada did not mention this addition, which Ma'mar alone narrated, indicating his error and mistake in it. An explanation of that follows: The hadith was narrated by Ibn Sa'd (), Ahmad (), 'Abd ibn Humaid (), al-Firyabi (), Abu Ya'la (), Ibn Hibban (1) via Sulayman ibn al-Mughira. And it was also narrated by Ibn Sa'd (13), Ahmad (13), 'Abd ibn Humaid (14), al-Bukhari (15), Muslim (1), al-Firyabi (17), Abu Ya'la (18), Ibn Khuzayma (19), Ibn Hibban (20), (1),
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage provides a practical example of how scholars identify an erroneous addition (زيادة خطأ) in a hadith. The author begins with a 'faaida' explaining al-Shafi'i's position on hand placement, then moves to the example. The hadith in question describes the Prophet making water flow from his fingers. Ma'mar ibn Rashid narrated it with the addition 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah). The author argues that this addition is mistaken because many other trustworthy narrators (Thabit, Qatada, and others via different chains) did not include it. The method is: if a single reliable narrator adds something that contradicts the majority of equally or more reliable narrators, that addition is considered erroneous (shadhdh or munkar). The author lists multiple chains (Sulayman ibn al-Mughira, etc.) that omit the phrase, proving Ma'mar's error. This is a standard technique in hadith criticism (al-jarh wa al-ta'dil and 'ilal al-hadith).

Key Terms
زيادة خطأ (ziyādah khaṭaʾ): An addition in a hadith that is proven erroneous because it contradicts the narration of more reliable or numerous narrators.
تفرد به (tafarrada bihi): To be alone in narrating an addition, which indicates weakness if opposed by others.
